12/27/23:
	-With our dragon dealt with, we set about addressing some immediate concerns.
		-I asked "Ship's Engineer Jade" to address our acid damaged helm and decking.
		-Once that was underway, I then turned to Maya, saying, "We. . . should probably send a
		  message to your father, what with that even bigger dragon on it's way to Sasserine. . ."
			-I provided some pointers as to what our strategy here should be, then went to go help
			 Jade with the helm.
			-She sent:
				"Daddy!! There is a Dragon incoming towards the city. It is beyond a size I have
				 ever seen, black and seems intent to destroy the city."
				"It is after the pearl, it sent a smaller kin against us and we just defeated it.
				 Ah for these last two messages: Raspberry Cupkake!!"
				"We will do our very best to destroy the Pearl through the portal-thing and hope
				 the Dragon will lose interest in you. Raspberry Cupcacke"
				"If all looks bleak for you and Sasserine, tell it about us, maybe it will be more
				 interested in us and ignore Sasserine. raspberry cupcake!"
				"Fredrick wants you to wait with this, but dont. Your life and the citizens are
				 more important than our lives Rasperry Cupcake. Love you....always."
			-Some scowling from me ensued when I returned and read that last bit she had written,
			 over her shoulder.
	-Jade's work plus some assistance from D'Roc and I got the helm back in working order, so I then
	 took control of the ship and got us back on our previous heading, towards the source of the
	 pearl's power.
	-A short while later, we heard back from Sasserine, in the form of Skye's penmanship.
		-It said:
			"Your father is going to take refuge in the vault of the bank, I am going to take
			 command of his men and draw the dragon to the arena. Let's hope neither place becomes
			 a tomb before you all return."
		-Huh. I thought Maya's father had better judgment than that, giving Skye command of troops.
		 He seems skeptical of _me_, after all, which I can't really fault. Then again, were
		 (another, bigger) dragon on it's way towards me, I wouldn't mind being in a bank vault
		 instead of out in front of some troops too. . .
		-They had some further back and forth too:
			"Do any of you know how to kill a black dragon?"
			"A Dragon on the ground is more vulnarable than in the air, try to harm/trap the wings
			 under things? It spits acid in an area."
			"What could it be searching for beneath the waters outside the city?"
			"The pearl? It might not know that we have it."
	-Well, that's mostly out of our hands, and our contribution needed to be racing to that portal.
		-So, while I kept the ship on it's earlier heading, Jade and Maya worked on picking up the
		 magic trail again.
		-They seemed to be struggling a bit with it, giving me intermittent, and occasionally
		 contradictory, directions.
			-It got somewhat better once they had Pook vomit up the pearl itself.
	-Meanwhile, I took a look through the spyglass, towards Sasserine, and saw the dragon hovering
	 over the city's harbor, the water beneath it pushed away with each wingbeat, inundating the
	 city. In the cavity  formed in the water, I could see tentacles emerging from it. . .
		-That warranted another book-message from Maya:
			"There are tentacles coming up from the water outside the city and there is a tsumami
			 wave coming towards you. Cover yourself."
		-And an alarming response:
			"You have a demogorgon coming for you."
		-Or, as Maya keeps referring to it, "Gummy Bear"
			-Admittedly, she's had some issues with bad things happening when she utters the names
			 of demons.
		-Sure enough, Maya looked again through the glass and saw a two-headed, tentacled ape-demon
		 racing through the air towards us, though Jade doubted it was Demogorgon _itself_, saying,
		 "I doubt the demon prince himself is actually here. Probably an avatar. . . though that's
		  plenty bad."
		-That prompted some scrambling.
			-We had Pook swallow the pearl again, which did indeed seem to cause the demon to
			 meander a bit more, trying to follow a fainter trail.
			-Sarge also ran to the caged air elementals, supercharging them with a spell and giving
			 the ship's speed a boost.
	-That speed boost kept the distance between us and the demon steady, but also seemed to be in
	 danger of ripping the ship apart.
		-I was shouting and directing my crew to tie down various things, adjust the sails, and the
		 like, while Jade and Maya frantically tried to keep the improvised repairs together.
		-We were rapidly approaching a small island chain, with some ruined obsidian temples fast
		 becoming visible on the islands, presumably our destination.
	-I was barely in control of the ship at this point and, calling for all the sail adjustments
	 and air elemental action I could to slow things down, I aimed her for the water, hoping for a
	 gentle(ish?) splashdown and that our hull was still intact enough to not take on water.
		-Maya, meanwhile, called her wings into being, grabbed Pook, and lept overboard, soon
		 followed by a potion-chugging Jade.
		-The rest of us hung on tight as the ship hit the water with an impressively graceful splash,
		 some couple hundred feet or so from shore.
		-The ship didn't seem to be taking on water, but also wasn't really meant to maneuver in it.
		-Nonetheless, I attempted to improvise, shouting to those still aboard to, "Reef the lower
		  sails, and angle the mainsail starboard, to catch the breeze!"
		-They attempted to comply, with D'Roc's tremendous strength going a long ways as he
		 descended below decks to pull on the now-disconnected spars controlling some of the lower
		 sails.
		-Between us, we got the ship about 50 feet out from the island, before something snapped and
		 one of the lower sails swung out again, arresting our progress.
		-"Well, I guess we're swimming for it!" D'Roc said, as he lept overboard.
		-I was not about to follow him into the water, a plan that proved wise as the armored man-
		 minotaur proceeded to sink like a stone.
		-"Man overboard!" I called, as I ran to fetch a rope, tying one end to the rail and the
		 other into a loop and tossing it to the bubbles marking D'Roc's last known location.
		-Maya and Bruce also flew over, diving into the water in an attempt to rescue D'Roc.
		-After a fraught few seconds, I felt a tug on the rope, so I wrapped the slack around the
		 anchor chain's winch and began winding it to pull them up.
		-Eventually, all three emerged from the water, and I helped them back aboard the ship.
		-Jade, seeing us all back above the waves, waved at us and pointed to one of the temples,
		 then ran inside.
		-I wasn't about to get in that water myself, so I fetched a few lengths of rope, tied them
		 together, and handed one end to Maya, saying, "Here! Tie this to something on the island
		 while I anchor the other to the ship."
		-We did just that, and soon the three of us still aboard ship without wings were dragging
		 ourselves hand-over-hand along the rope and through the water.
	-Back on dry land, we all followed Jade into that dank, ruined temple.
		-Shortly inside the temple's entrance, though, Bruce called a halt, whispering, "There are
		  voices ahead, around the bend. They're speaking Abyssal, I think. . ."
		-So, we set about performing some (quiet) preparations, Jade healing several of the others
		 while I manifested my precognition.
		-Jade claimed we needed to toss the pearl through the portal, and we began whispered
		 discussion of how to accomplish that.
		-It was interrupted by a thud from behind us.
			-Something hitting the temple's door. Something enormous. . .
		-A moment later, two tentacles smashed through the doors and I started running.
		-Hero that I am, I drew my bow as I did so and loosed an arrow behind me. It pierced one of
		 the tentacles through the center of it's mass and that one withdrew with a sharp jerk.
		-Sarge ran _towards_ them, bravely (but unwisely) hurling spells.
		-Bruce, Grimble, and Pook, though, more prudently ran forward into the tunnel.
		-Grimble, clearly looking to facilitate that, conjured a garguntuan gold dragon, barely
		 small enough to squeeze down the corridor, which he made run down the corridor, roaring
		 and snapping it's jaws.
		-Knowing his specialty and taking his cue, I joined in the fun, yelling, "Get 'em, Gortrax!
		  Kill anything that moves!"
		-Maya began to blast away at the remaining tentacle. Jade dragged her further into the
		 tunnel to as D'Roc ran past them, lopping the end of the tentacle off with his axe,
		 splattering him and Sarge with green goo.
		-I skidded to a halt at the bend in the corridor and cautiously peered past the corner of
		 the wall.
			-Past the (illusion of a) dragon and at the end of the corridor, I could see some kind
			 of winged creature in a cage, being tormented by a swarm of locusts.
		-As the others caught up with me, a demon of some kind emerged from a doorway on the left
		 of the corridor I was looking down. . . and began to "fight" the illusory dragon.
		-Motion down the corridor I came from _also_ then caught my eye. D'Roc was charging at
		 Grimble and I!
			-He had a crazy look in his eyes, and seemed to struggle with himself, but kept his
			 axe lowered.
		-Well, I wanted no part of that, so I dashed past my fellows, towards the dragon illusion
		 and further into the temple.
			-I ended up taking cover in a niche across from the door the demon had emerged from.
			-Through that doorway, I could see more demons, pouring out from a portal. . .
		-"Portal-ho!" I yelled, as I loosed an arrow at the nearby demon. The arrow. . . missed,
		  flying through the tail of the "dragon".
		-The demon saw that, stared at the dragon for a moment, and then turned it's back to the
		 dragon and ran back through the door it came from.
		-Sarge and Bruce then ran forward, over to the dragon, as Grimble ran up next to me.
		-Sarge loosed some kind of energy down the corridor while Bruce conjured more snowfall
		 around himself, providing welcome concealment.
		-Belowing somewhere through the snow, I could hear some demonic voice shouting in their
		 foul language.
		-That was soon joined by Grimble screaming, off to my left, but I couldn't see anything
		 through the snow.
		-Fortunately, the snow soon ceased in part of the room we were in (perhaps Bruce moved his
		 spell, as it continued to snow through the door to the South), revealing Grimble running
		 towards me with a gaping axe wound and a still-crazed D'Roc some distance behind him.
		-He still managed to move his dragon forward into the snow, and Jade rushed after it.
		-Maya approached the D'Roc and tried to talk him down from whatever was going one, reminding
		 him he'd sworn an oath to her father to protect her. It did seem to get through to him, as
		 he slouched, and let his axe fall from his hands.
		-Keeping a wary eye on D'Roc, watching for sudden movements, I sidled over to Grimble and
		 healed him with my magic belt as he did the same with his.
		-Through the snow, I heard a muffled, "Pook is a good boy!" and then there was a big "fwoop"
		 as the snow was blasted away and I was pressed against the wall by the pressure.
		-There, through the doorway, I could see the portal was now gone, and an armless Pook slowly
		 collapsed to the ground.
		-The temple, though, also felt like it was in danger of joining him in that. The burst of
		 air may have done some damage, or there might be some more magical explanation. Either way,
		 it was shaking as stones began to fall from the corridor's ceiling.
		-Grimble quickly barked a few arcane syllables, shrinking to tiny baby size, and I scooped
		 him up and made for the door at Hasted speeds.
		-The others, less wisely, ran the other direction, as Maya shouted, "We need to save the
		  prisoners!"
	-Soon, I stood panting outside the temple's exterior door, holding Grimble, and twenty seconds
	 later, the rest of the party, save poor Pook, emerged, along with. . . some kind of rainbow-
	 winged serpent, a strange winged humanoid, and a giant ant.
		-"You guys made it!" I cried out, ". . . Along with. . . are those more demons?"
		 "No, my child," a. . . voice in my head said, "I was their prisoner, and you saved me."
		 "Oh. Well, that's good, then."
		-Maya then made an entreaty, asking the rescued prisoner for help in saving her city of
		 Sasserine.
		-They said they'd be honored to help, and so we fell to discussing the logistics of that.
			-As the disembodied voice (the winged serpent, I think?) rightfully pointed out, _some_
			 of us could fly, but the others would need some way to get there.
			-I quickly conferred with Jade, but neither of us had a way to repair the ship sooner
			 than a week.
			-The serpent volunteered that it could take us to another plane, but not easily around
			 _this_ plane.
			 "Could you take us to another plane and back to Sasserine?" Jade asked.
			 "It is. . . not that accurate," it responded. "I could take you to Sigil, maybe? The
			  city of doors? It's renowned for it's portals."
			 "Does it. . . have bars?" I asked.
			 "More than can be counted."
			 "Alright! That's the plan for me!"
			-The others were still insistent on a route back to Sasserine, though, so the serpent
			 then volunteered that it could fly somewhere and fetch us a scroll or the like.
			-"Well," I volunteered, "There's the goblins?"
			 "You have goblins?" the serpent asked.
			 "And a spare ship too!"
			-I described for the creature where I'd left the goblins and their airship, saying,
			 "Tell them Fred needs a ride, and that there's good booze in it for them!"
			-We went with that, though Maya was not content to wait, and took off after the serpent,
			 flying a good deal slower, but heading the same direction.
	-Soon enough, I could see the goblin's derigible hanging above the horizon, and heading for us.
		-They took us aboard and we headed back to Sasserine.
	-There, we found a city devestated by the dragon atack: buildings clawed, drenched in acid, or
	 damaged by flooding, and bodies in the streets.
		-We eventually found Skye, who the city's people were hailing as a hero for driving off the
		 dragon.
			-I asked him how that felt, but he glowered, and replied, "Don't talk to me. For several
			 days."
				-I shrugged, grabbed a wine bottle from my pack, and began drinking, sharing with
				 those around me.
				-One of the Dracus house guards I offered a swig to gestured to Skye, saying Skye
				 nearly died in the battle with the dragon, but that they rivived him.
					-That might explain Skye's dark mood, given his glorification of death. Though
					 there's also Pook's demise, strangers talking to him, and many other Skye-
					 annoyances.
				-Maya insisted on trying to give Skye some kind of pep talk, but I quickly wandered
				 off.
		-We then dispersed from there, each of us helping the city and it's residents in our own
		 ways.
			-I did some light looting, wandering the streets drinking and grabbing refills as needed.
				-I pressed many of those I passed to have a drink too, with mixed results as the
				 city's populace each mourned their ills in their own ways.
		-In the immediate aftermath, the next few days, there was lots of rebuilding, and other
		 changes.
			-House Dracus's power in the city surged, as it's lord emerged unharmed from the bank
			 and he and Maya both took leading roles in rebuilding.
				-Maya even reached out to the king of Sharaar Kol, asking for the assistance of
				 it's dwarven craftsmen. They came after a few days, and assisted greatly in the
				 process.
				-I also heard her discussing with Sarge the rebuilding of the city's defenses.
					-He had offered to help train new soldiers, and she also asked him if any like
					 him would be willing to come take service with the city too. They made plans
					 to seek out other dragonborn veterans and hire them as mercenaries.
			-My own name ended up cleared too, as all of us were hailed as heroes of the city.
				-They insisted on no speeches, though.
				-"Fine, fine. . ." I replied. "How about a toast, then?"
			-Jade went and saw to her adoptive family of orphans, funding and assisting in the
			 construction of another structure for the orphanage.
			-D'Roc too did some construction, putting his (enormous) back into it, and picking up
			 some carpentry skills.
			-After the first day or three of binge drinking I. . . well, I kept drinking, but did
			 a lot of talking with the various members of the city's populace.
				-I talked up the air-sailing lifestyle, and the wonders of my own adventures.
			-My airship, though, was a more or less total loss.
				-We salvaged what we could of it and, with all the set aside funds in the ship's
				 account, plus some more out of our own pockets, we set Jade to building a new one.

1/10/23: A brief session, handling some of the details of our long downtime.
	-I helped Jade negotiate some deals for a magic shop she set up during our year in Sasserine.
		-She also did some humanitarian activities along the way, especially in the days following
		 the dragon attack, crafting magic items to help, like a decanter providing endless fresh
		 water.
		-She also put together a magic lute that builds stuff, which Maya put to good (and good
		 sounding) use.
		-And, of course, she put together our new ship, even making some improvements for
		 _cooperative_ elementals crewing it.
			-Fantasy Grounds now has some Airship maps, with a fancy interior.
	-Sarge left Sasserine for much of the year, in search of further arcane learning.
		-He came back with tales of not _too_ distant locales, like Glyphstone Keep, the city of
		 Wroat with it's many magical wonders, and the volcano he visited.
	-D'Roc, on the other hand, hung around Sasserine. Between his prodigious strength and,
	 apparently, some carpentry experience, he was a lot of help with rebuilding the city.
		-I also heard him and Maya discussing the mystery of his origins, with her helping him do
		 some research on the subject.
		-He did a bit of a field trip for that too, going off alone into the wilds outside the city.
			-He came back calm and confident.
	-Maya, meanwhile, busied herself with politics.
		-The Dawn Council's power, in the wake of this disaster, had really waned. She spent a lot
		 of time pushing for changes to the city's government, with an eye to more of a voice for
		 the city's common people.
	-As for myself. . .
		-The city's party scene was something of a disappointment for the first few months after
		 the attack.
		-Nonetheless, where no party is to be found, I can create one, and I set about doing (a lot
		 of) just that!
		-During the day, though, most of the city busied itself with rebuilding, a process I watched
		 a lot of when I was awake for it.
		-While roaming one of the construction sites, I spotted the one, the only Party Lizard,
		 carrying lumber.
			-"Party Lizard!" I called out. "How have you been?!?"
			 "Fred! I've been good. These elves I'm here with are really chill."
			 "You'll have to introduce me! Let me find some wine. . ."
			 "Ah," he replied, "What I could really go for is some of those sausages. . . Do you
			  remember?"
			 "Oh yeah! What was that bar. . . Oh! The Lusty Leper!"
			 "Yeah, that place was great! I wonder if it's still standing. . . Well, there's one fun
			  way to find out!"

	-In the lead up to Founders Day, and a party I planned to host for it, I heard a voice in my

		-"A chosen of mystra said I should rendevous with all of you to return the piece of mt.

		-There, Bruce volunteeered that he had a handy spell to trigger a portal but, before he

	-We found ourselves on what I at first presumed to be an island. . . until I saw its head and
	 fins.
		-In fact, we stood on vegetation-clad back of an enormous turtle, as several others swam
		 in the water nearby.
		-Well, Lucien wasted little time, and began to hack away at the giant like the tree it was
		 the size of.
		-All of us joined in on that, though after some conjured flame and bow, I, with Grimble
		 strapped to me, dove into some turtle-bushes, to get out of sight.
		-That proved quickly prudent, as one of the smaller-but-still enormous turtles emerged from
		 the water, clambering up the back of it's bigger fellow and interposing itself between us
		 and the giant.
		-At that sight, Sarge took a few steps back, saying, "Guys. . . we should try talking this
		 out. . . I think it's a _good_ turtle."
		 "Well," mumbled Bruce, "I do think I might speak it's language. . ."
		 "Yeah! Talk him down from this ledge, Bruce!" I yelled out, from my bush. "Let him know
		  that getting rid of this thing should stop all the portals. He probably hates that! I
		  know I would, in my living room. . ."
		-Bruce, in a burbly, liquid-y language, began to speak to the turtle.
		-And, as it turned out, not a moment too soon, as I felt myself lose my control of the
		 giant's mind. It felt like the turtle had. . . intervened, somehow.
		-Bruce did, though, seem to get through to the beast. It nodded to him, than pushed itself
		 backward with its fins, back into the water.
		-The now-stirring giant was then immediately subjected more attacks from the party.
		-A hail of conjured rocks from Sarge saw particular succes, and he called out that, "It's
		  vulnerable to the element of Earth!"
		-"Alright, then," I whispered to Grimble. "On my signal. . . One. . . Two. . ."
		-I then popped up from the bushes, loosing several arrows at the giant, striking it twice
		 in the chest.
		-Grimble followed that by, from my chest, tossing a thimble-sized green vial. One that grew
		 as it flew forth from his hand and struck the giant, splattering all over it.
		-The giant sizzled, popped, and. . .dissolved into lightning.
			-A neat trick. . . if it weren't for the fact that I'm pretty sure he's dead now.
		-That lightening, though, dispersed into the turtle beneath us, and the water around it, and
		 the turtle began to shudder.
		-"You're welcome!" I called out, to the other turtle, and then scurried over to Jade, saying,
		 "Lets get the fuck out of here.
		-She complied and, after joining hands with all of us, she snapped the weird device The
		 Chosen had given us. Suddenly. . .
	-We were on The Material once more.
		-The Chosen of Mystra stood before us and, undisturbed by our sudden appearance, she said,
		 "You've succceeded, I see. You have my thanks."
		-Indeed, through the doorway, what once was chaotic swirls and a snow dusted rocky slope was
		 now, well, still a chaotic glowing river of. . . something, but different than it was a short
		 while ago!
		-"So," The Chosen continued, "We should then see to your rewards. . ."
		-As promised, she gave Lucien and I each a book, entitled the Tome of Experience.
			-I frowned a bit, but placed it in my pack. I am my best asset after all, so I suppose
			 I can stomach a self-help book.
		-To Sarge, she handed a staff made of brass and a bronze-colored wood, after a wave of her
		 hand summoned or called it into being.
			-That evidently delighted him.
		-And, to Jade, she similarly called for a beautiful piece of crystal, saying, "This should
		  suit your purposes. I shall also give you the time you need with the stream. Go, child,
		  and do your working."
			-Jade made some preparations, taking a seat beside the stream and drawing circles and
			 diagrams around herself with various magical reagents.
			-Then, slowly, she dipped one corner of the crystal into the stream. . . and went still.
			-We waited moments. . . then minutes, and still she did not withdraw the crystal from
			 the stream or otherwise move.
			-After a fair while of growing more agitated by the moment, Bruce approached and tried
			 to reach for the crystal. . . only to also go still when _he_ touched it.
			-Well, the rest of us looked at each other. . . but then sat down to wait a while
			 without attempting further interventions.
			-After what had to have been a couple of hours, Jade and Bruce both stirred.
			-Jade, in particular, looked somewhat shaken, but also reported success. She also said
			 she thought it will be a bit healthier than the other too. . .

2/21/24:
	-Reality untangled, we made our way back out of the mines and to the dwarven city.
	-A 10 ft. tall bull-man proved easy to find in a city of dwarves, especially since they were at
	 my first stop, the bar I left my party-goers at.
		-(I wasn't even looking for them yet. Just wanted a drink. . .)
		-Greeting them, Jade inquired how Maya and D'Roc's hob-nobbing went.
		-Sounds like they met with success, and came back with some potential work.
			-Apparently there's some issues with bandits, and Maya came up with some plan to settle
			 them on some empty land to resolve the issue. The king was amenable and she got the job
			 of talking them into it, and getting them to a meeting about it.
			 "Sell them on it being more fun to hang with Fred than getting impaled?" I asked. "Seems
			  pretty easy."
		-Jade had also apparently had a dream recently, concerning some of Nikisi's followers in The
		 Morticians Guild.
			-She thought it meant they were still around, and wanted to go haring off after them.
			-Weirdly, Lucien was backing her on this, acting like he was _there_, in her dream. . .
				-Well, I've heard, seen, and done crazier. . .
			-Not sure I want anything further to do with followers of The Brotherhood, but I also
			 guess we'd probably be killing those corpsefuckers.
		-We debated the subject briefly, but Lucien took the. . . higher? wetter? ground, and poured
		 out two shots of his Abyssal liquor.
			-He passed one to D'Roc, saying, "I don't believe you've tried this yet. . ."
			-I never knew D'Roc to lack bravery (though I've also never much loved Wisdom), yet he
			 seemed reluctant to try the strange liquor, having seen it's effect on the rest of us,
			 resisting even as I began to chant, "Drink! Drink! Drink!"
			-Lucien shrugged, and then downed both shots, leading to much raving on Lucien's part.
				-Jade even pointed out that he seemed to suffer from some sinister spell effect,
				 though there was some disagreement about exactly what amount the arcanely inclined.
				-They bandied about sinister terms like "Power Word" or "Phantasmal Killer".
				-Whatever it was, it gave Lucien a hell of a nosebleed.
		-As Lucien came back around, we coalesced on the bandit task.
		-I felt no need to _hurry_ out into the wilderness, and said as much, suggesting we order a
		 round and some food, then make plans.
			-In particular, I suggested we talk about what supplies we need to stock up on.
			-On the walk back to the city, Jade and I had discussed options for helping me focus a
			 bit better, especially after I almost lost my grip on that lighting elemental/giant's
			 mind. She had actually had a great suggestion, some spell for the rythmically-inclined
			 which she could create a wand of for me, and even extend the wand's duration as she'd
			 been doing with other spells already. I was sold, and wanted to pick up the materials
			 for it.
	-Dinner(? Hard to tell when undergound. . .) done with, we did our shopping, then headed back
	 to the ship, chivvying some of my stray followers aboard as we ran into them.
		-Once back to the ship, I sent some of the followers on hand to round up the rest, and put
		 the others already there to loading the ship.
		-Soon, we were aloft.
	-The ship traveled through the night and, the next day, we were soon in the area we'd been told
	 the bandits were operating.
		-Jade, with some help from her magic crystal, was able to create that Undersong wand for me
		 while we traveled.
		-I suggested that, to find the bandits, we engage in some aerial reconnaissance (in no small
		 part because I got to sit aboard my comfortable ship while we did so).
		-The party all assented, and Lucien and Bruce climbed the mast to keep lookout in the crow's
		 nest.
		-A little while later, some commotion came from the top of the mast, with Bruce and Lucien
		 yelling.
		-I looked up just in time to see a bolt of lightening strike the mast.
		-Looking in the direction it came from, I saw a huge winged lizard and, casting my eyes
		 about, I spotted another nearby.
		-Grimble dived behind a gunwale and began casting a spell on himself while one of the winged
		 lizards swooped at the crows nest, attempting to claw at Lucien as Lucien ducked.
		-Battle was joined and, as the lizards swooped again and again at Lucien (he seemed to be
		 taking pains to draw attention to himself) while our party hurled spells back at them.
		-I focused on one of them and froze it's brain. It's outstretched wings kept it at a gentle
		 glide but it rapidly fell behind our speeding ship.
		-Meanwhile, D'Roc rushed to the front of the ship and brought one of our loaded cannons to
		 bear on the remaining lizards, shooting it out of the sky.
		-That left the brain locked lizard, which soon shook the effect off as the ship pulled me
		 out of the range of my power, after which it began flapping after us.
		-It was somewhat faster than the ship and was slowly closing the distance, so the whole
		 party joined me at the back of the ship, readying attacks for when it got back in range.
		-Noteably, D'Roc dragged the two remaining loaded cannons over, with seeming ease, which
		 he and Lucien quickly made good use of as the winged thing neared.
		-That was joined by a variety of spells and other projectiles.
		-Sarge flew forward, to get the thing in range of a spell, but that proved a pit unwise
		 when the thing swooped forward and grabbed Sarge with it's claws.
		-Maya took wing too, flying closer to the beast, and shot it straight in the face,
		 vaporizing its head with eldritch energy.
		-Sarge was then able to quickly free himself from the now limp claws, and I slowed the ship
		 while he and Maya flapped back over.
	-Some healing and reloading followed.
		-Lucien asked if we were ready to continue on or if we should rest, to which I replied, "I'm
		 ready for a toast! To our victory!" Lucien obligingly poured out some whiskey shots.
		-The warming whiskey was well welcome, as the sun had to dropped nearly to the horizon, the
		 temperature dropping with it.
		-The twilight was very welcome too, though, as it was essentially the perfect time to search
		 for bandits.
	-Before the sun had set, Lucien called out from the crows nest, saying, "A caravan! And it's in
	  trouble. . ."
		-Climbing down, he pointed out the caravan. . . and it's pursuers. "They're rather large. . ."
		 he added.
		-I changed the ship's heading and soon we were hovering above the caravan, perhaps 15 or 20
		 feet up.
		-Lucien wasted no time jumping down to the ground, landing with a graceful roll, and was
		 followed shortly by D'Roc, landing with a thud.
		-In response the bandits, now clearly _ogre_ bandits, took off running.
		-Lucien growled at them to halt, and they did, while Maya flew down and started talking to
		 them.
		-She asked them questions about how many of them there were, and eventually arranged to
		 meet with their leader, back at the cave in which their tribe of bandits resided.
		-The caravan, meanwhile, was guarded by a party of more junior adventurers.
			-We accepted their thanks, and Maya offered them the blessings of of Bahamut, a thing
			 that delighted all of them, save one dressed in black who grumbled in response.
			-Lucien offered one, a ranger, a swig of the Abyssal Temptation, which he took like a
			 champ.
			-(They're all level two, except the ranger, who leveled up from bravely facing The
			  Abyss.)
	-I instructed my followers to, after we left, bring the ship up higher until they caught sight
	 of us again, and admonished them to listen to Rusty. The rest of us, then, descended via ropes
	 and various other means, and followed the ogres back to their cave.
		-They led us back to a filthy cavernmouth, and inside.
		-Just inside the entrance, they halted. Looking from one to another, they then turned to us,
		 giggling, of all things, and asked, "Uh, do you like surprises?"
		-That understandably met with a chorus of no's from us, and rather spoiled the surprise when
		 an enormous ball of writhing black ooze dropped down onto us.
		-Sarge's reflexes were quick and he seared it with a blast of flame from his hands as it
		 fell, but fell it still did, right on Lucien.
		-That was like spitting a loogie into a blender, though, Lucien with his sword and all, and
		 we were all sprayed by bits of it. . . annoyingly damaging a lot of our equipment with the
		 acidic slime.
		-Lucien continued on, slaying one of the ogres too.
		-I called out to the remaining one, "Here's a surprise: I'd be surprised if you live through
		  this. Better cut this surprise shit _really_ fast. . ."
		-He cowered, in response, and Lucien demanded, "Now, who was your leader?"
		-Maya then stepped forward and chimed in, "My friends here _do not_ like surprises. Take us
		  to your leader without any more of them. . ."
		 "Bu. . . But, he said people _love_ survivors. . ." the ogre blubbered, as he turned and
		 walked off down the tunnel.
	-The remaining ogre led us a ways through the caves without further incident, and eventually to
	 a chamber bedecked in carved stone and featuring a man in dark furs, a statue behind him, and
	 a floor carpeted in a mix of treasure and bones.
		-"Did you get the caravan?" he began in response to the ogre's thudding footfalls. "It
		  should ha. . ."
		-As he trailed off at the sight of us behind the ogre, the ogre gestured to him, saying,
		 "This Ravenshroud. He good leader. . ."
		 ". . . What in the hells do you want?" Ravenshroud then said, addressing us. "I see I now
		  seem to be short an ogre. . ."
		-Maya launched into her spiel, saying she came with an offer from the king of Sharaar Kol,
		 an offer of peace, land, and alliance, if he would stop his depredations.
		-He nodded along, saying "Uh huh, I would be willing. . ."
		-I, though, detected a note in his voice. He sounded concerned and evasive, like he was
		 getting ready to bolt.
		-Indeed, following his arm down, I saw him reaching for a lever alongside his statue. . .
		-Acting quickly to forestall. . . whatever he was doing, I unleashed a blast of psionic
		 energy, stunning the bandit leader. . . along with most of my party, and the ogre.
		-D'Roc, though, was behind me, and outside the effect of the blast, while Lucien also
		 seemed to resist it.
		-I had both of them quickly help me, to drag Ravenshroud away from his lever, to snap off
		 the lever, and to pull Maya out from the space between the bandit and his ogre.
		-After only a few moments, the stunned folks began stirring.
		-Ravenshroud came to with Lucien and D'Roc standing over him. As the bandit unsteadily
		 clambered to his feet, Lucien growled, "That could have gone a lot worse. . ."
		 "Yeah," I added, "We could just as easily have slit your throat while you were on the
		  ground. . . Try listening this time. . . or we'll try that."
		-Clearly, he got the message, and he was much more receptive to _Maya's_ message.
			-She soon had him agreeing to meet with the king, and had even offered him a ride back
			 to Sharaar Kol with us, aboard our luxurious airship.
			-She _did_ note, though, that his ill-gotten plunder might need to be confiscated, a
			 thing the rest of us enthusiastically set about doing as she led him off down the
			 tunnel, towards the cave's entrance.

3/6/24:
	-I spent the flight back to Sharaar Kol drinking with Lucien, D'Roc, and the bandit leader.
		-We all pushed the idea of taking the king's deal pretty hard.
			-"You can go legit!" I suggested. "Now, you 'confiscate' 'taxes' from caravans!"
		-He sampled some of Lucien's Abyssal liquor, followed by Lucien himself, and they both
		 began babbling about the contents of their shoulders.
			-Interestingly, they fell to discussing some past deal of the bandit's, mentioning a
			 drow named "Raith", who had set him up in his current deal, inducing him to attack
			 caravans in the area, and providing weapons and goons with which to do so.
			-It suggests there's another power in play here, and one that might work against our
			 bandit's change of heart and Sharaar Kol's interests.
			-"Well," I told the bandit, "Sounds like the dwarf king's got another problem, and us
			  an opportunity, problem solvers that we are."
		-We also explained to him that Maya is big in Sasserine. Being on her good side could mean
		 some backing from another power.
	-Once back at Sharaar Kol, Maya offered to take the bandit king to an inn to freshen up, and to
	 go find some nicer clothes for his meeting with the dwarven king.
		-So, we started talking about shopping!
		-Jade chimed in that she might have a way to fund some of that shopping: salt.
			-Apparently, she can conjure the stuff, and asked for our help selling it in bulk, here
			 and maybe other ports of call.
				-She demonstrated this talent by first conjuring some huge rock bins in the ship's
				 hold and then conjuring the salt itself, inside the bins and in vast quantity.
				-Supposedly, she said, 10's of _thousands_ of gold worth.
			-Interesting possibilities, here!
				-"Our problem, then," I said, "Is one of demand, not supply. But, we've got our ship,
				  and already visit plenty of ports of call. . ."
				-Maya even volunteered that one of the other noble families in Sasserine run the
				 city's fishing industry. . .
			-So, we got to selling, clearing 2700 gp. with a single bulk sale.
		-We then set about unloading our confiscated-from-the-bandits loot and replacing our acid
		 damaged stuff.
			-Maya bought some _elaborate_ clothes for herself, Jade, Sarge, and D'Roc.
	-Shopping handled, we then went to see the king, bringing the bandit along.
		-The bandit leader, hesitent and seemingly shy before the dwarf king, related the tale of
		 this drow Raith. Maya eventually had to help him along, offering some of the details
		 herself.
		-The king had little respect for the suddenly shy bandit, provoking him rather badly, but
		 the bandit remained meek and agreed to the king's terms.
			-In particular, given the revelation about this drown backer, the dwarf king doubted
			 (aloud) that the (former) bandit could really hold this land.
		-We, in turn, were paid a princely sum, 4,000 gp., for delivering and convincing the man.
		-We were also offered a new task: bringing to the king this drow.
			-After the way the last task paid, we were happy to accept.
	-When we were dismissed from the king's presence, we set about discussing our drow hunt, and
	 the supplies we'd need.
		-The now-former bandit interjected, "Well, you guys _broke_ the lever to The Underdark. . ."
		-That got us all staring at him, and he went on to explain that the lever had been the
		 start of the long, twisting path through The Underdark that he had been following to meet
		 his drow contact.
			-"I think it was such a long mess just because he liked torturing me. . ." he added.
			-This was so helpful we bothered to ask his name: Gevin.

		-So, with just paid-for crafting time, through the magic crystal and Lesser Restoration,
		 it costs:
			-Wand charges: 20/50*562.5 = 225 gp. and 20/50*60 = 24 XP
			-Stone: 10k*.75 = 7.5k and 20k/25 = 800 XP
			-For a total of: 7,725 gp. and 824 XP

		http://mcdt2-dungeon.wikidot.com/item:vest-of-resistance
		https://www.dandwiki.com/wiki/SRD:Ring_of_Protection
	-Jade craft formula:
		Gold: COST_IN_GP/2*.75
		XP: COST_IN_GP/25
		Time: Floor(COST_IN_GP/1000)
				or
			  WAND_CHARGES_IN_GP = Floor(COST_IN_GP/1000)*1500/50
			  Crafting cost: WAND_CHARGES_IN_GP/2*.75 gp., WAND_CHARGES_IN_GP/25 in XP
				Lessor Restoration as a 1st lvl. paladin wand is 1500
				The crystal can provide 1 day worth of time per charge, as it removes Fatigued
				(or turns Exhausted to Fatigued) and the crystal does:
					"First 10 minutes = Fatigued, then Exhausted after another 10"
	-So a Vest of Resistance +3:
		9000/2*.75 = 3375 gp., 9000/25 = 360 XP
		Wand charges = 9000/1000 = 9
			WAND_CHARGES_IN_GP = 9*1500/50 = 270 gp.
			Crafting cost: 270/2*.75 = 101.25 gp. ; 270/25 = 10.8


3/20/24:
	-The drow hunting discussion continued, and we quickly addressed the light aspect: Maya has
	 a dozen or so sunrods that we'll tie to D'Roc's horn as needed (most of us can see in the dark
	 anyways).
	-Far _less_ quickly, though, we discussed Jade's wonderous enchanting talents, kicked off by my
	 bringing up a luck rock I want.
		-She was amenable, having that magic crystal now, and she even offered to cover the magical
		 energies if I would purchase the materials.
		-That inspired a flurry of further requests, from the others and even another for me: a
		 shiny magic vest!
		-She was frantically noting down the details of our shouted-over-each-other commissions,
		 looking a bit harried, while Bruce hovered (not, in this case, literally) at her side,
		 looking a bit worried.
		-She paused then, suddenly and, looking up, said, ". . . How old will I be after this?"
		-We looked at her quizically and she elaborated. "This. . . accelerated time. . . it has
		  real, physical impacts on the world. Even with the fatigue handled by other magic, I
		  think I'm at least growing older by the days it grants me. . ."
		 ". . . Huh," I replied. "Well. . . you were going to build all this stuff anyways, right?
		  It's basically a wash for you! It's just better for us! Faster!"
		 "Uh. . ."
		-That sparked lots of conversation.
			-Bruce was asking her if, "young lady", she really thought this was worth it.
			-She, meanwhile and looking to the rest of us, sounded almost be pleading, "If we do
			  this. . . We'll find a way to fix this, right?"
			-I felt her exactly. "Sure! We'll just figure out how to make ourselves immortal!"
			-Then, after a pause, I added, "If you've got something for that. . . get working,
			 Jade."
			 "Uh. . ."
			-Since she was starting to seem a bit reluctant with all this, I offered something a
			 bit more concrete.
				-"Look," I said, "If it comes to it, I now a way you can become immortal. It's not
				  the _best_ option, but, if we can't find something better, it's there."
				 "Uh. . . how?" she asked.
				 "I _promise_. Isn't that good enough?"
				 ". . . No."
				 ". . . OK. Fine," I said, giving in. "It's the big thing where I come from. . .
				  People turning into these. .  . Elans, they call themselves. Then, they live
				  forever!"
				 "Where. . . What is. . ."
				 "It's tied to Edric, the god that made me."
				 ". . . Why haven't you done it?"
				 "Can't. The bastard. . ."
				 "Why not?"
				 "It's. . . You know how I can kill you with my brain?" I said. "It's got something
				  to do with that. Ed tried it with. . . someone he knew, way back. . . . I think
				  I'm actually related to the guy. He was like me, anyways, and, after the
				  process. . . Well, what's left of him is some kind of. . . mold? It covers miles
				  and miles. . . but is definitely not how I want to end up."
			-The conversation awkwardly petered out after that. . . but she agreed to all the
			 crafting.
	-That settled, we did various bits of shopping.
		-There were the enchanting materials, of course.
		-Maya also wanted to get some make up, "To make her look like a drow."
			-This was. . . questionable.
			-But, I wasn't going to stop her! In fact, "Sure, Maya! Let's go shopping! We'll bring
			 Grimble! He's in the _entertainment_ industry!"
			-And we did exactly that, with Maya spending 50 gold on the various cosmetics she,
			 Grimble, and I pointed at in the shop we visited.
		-From there, Maya also wanted to visit the high priest of Moradin, the one we'd saved from
		 that vile kidnapper. . . Nkondi.
			-After all, she pointed out that a dwarven priest is likely well able to help guard us
			 against those perfidious drow and the nefarious poisons.
			-Her name was plenty to get _her_ taken back to see the priest, a thing I made no real
			 attempt to shoehorn my way into, I not being in the mood to be preached at.
			-Instead, when she collected us in the nearby square, reporting that the priest had
			 promised her that he'd have an assortment of potions available for us inside of an
			 hour or two, I suggested we find a tavern in which to wait.
		-We then found a nearby bar, labeled the The Endless Bar and built into a disused mineshaft
		 with the other end of the space ending in a collapsed tunnel.
			-The barkeep greeted us and I ordered an ale.
			-He also offered some welcome food, a chicken and mushroom soup or the chef's special,
			 a roast mole.
				-"Well, you caught my ears with the mushroom, figure a dwarf would know good
			      mushrooms," I said. "But dwarves would know _moles_ too! I'll have the special!"
				-Sarge added that he'd have, "What the captain's having." Soon, the barkeep was
				 calling me captain too.
				 "Always good to see a tavern that's in ship-shape!" I graciously riffed.
		-A few hours turned into three or four and then the raucous bunch of us went to go pick up
		 the potions at the temple, with Maya taking possession of them.
	-All that in hand, we grabbed our bandit king from the dwarf king's residence and headed for
	 the ship.
		-Between our previous visit and the bandit's landmarks, it was no trouble to find our way
		 back to his cave and, descending, we were soon back in his. . . audience chamber.
		-Jade examined the broken lever and, with a moment's fiddling, was able to trigger it's
		 connected mechanism, sliding away a counterweighted stone wall and opening a passageway.
		-We then discussed directions with the bandit.
			-He said the dark elf changed the location he held the meetings regularly, but all were
			 reached at the end of a long, winding series of caverns.
			-In particular, he also mentioned an old, ruined temple, in which grew glowing green
			 mushrooms, where he had held their most important meetings.
			-We seized on that and got detailed directions to it. Between that and several of our
			 group being skilled trackers, we figured we had it covered.
	-Following the bandit's directions, we wound through caves for what felt like many hours, though
	 time was quite hard to guage down here.
	-Eventually, though, we reached a cave where, as it opened up a bit and we walked forward, dark,

3/25/24:

4/3/24:
	-Well, that druid is mostly blood-colored now, but he sure doesn't look like a drow.
		-Maybe an orc, looking at him.
		-In any event, he didn't seem to be our target.
	-But, first, we did take a moment to further examine our surroundings. . . and the late druid's
	 possessions.
		-It had sunk in for me that Bruce had mentioned some connection _to the element of earth_,
		 so, with mixed feelings, I asked him about it, saying, "So. . . you said something about
		  an 'Earth's End'? That where this druid was from?"
			-That kicked off further discussion of the subject, from which I gleaned a few things:
				-Earth's End is something of a trading post, located in The Underdark.
				-There is a portal there, connected to The Elemental Plane of Earth.
				-The glyphs on that carved bone sceptor described a path to the place, glyphs that
				 Bruce could decipher and which gave landmarks D'Roc was confident he'd be able to
				 find.
			-So, we could find the place if we wanted. But, I raised the question of _should_ we.
				-"Is this where we're going to try and find the drow? That abandoned temple or what
				  not?" I asked.
				-D'Roc and Bruce both conferred, and also looked over a nearby ledge, down into a
				 darkened cavern ahead of us.
				-They claimed they could see, below, a field of large glowing crystals, one of the
				 landmarks on _both_ routes, but said that, from there, the paths diverge.
				-"Well," I said, "The abandoned temple, where this drow was hosting meetings, that's
				  our goal here. What do you say we check the place out and, if that trail is cold,
				  hit up this trading post next, and ask around? How about it?"
				-That met with a chorus of nods, so that's what we resolved to do.
		-I also then brought up the glowing fungus, saying, "Anyone interested in those mushrooms
 		 over there? The ones that lit up in response to magic and my brain powers?"
			-That, though, found no takers, and I certainly wasn't going to touch the things myself.
	-With us having resolved to continue on to the abandoned temple, we set about looking for a way
     down to the floor of the cavern over the ledge, the one with the crystals we could see far below
	 us, glowing.
		-We discussed various options for getting down what proved to be a 200' sheer descent.
			-Several people could fly, and we had various things we could cast, but getting everyone
			 down with magic would certainly impose some degree of cost.

			  like the lazy sort. . . think there's some kind of path somewhere?"
		-That prompted a search, which eventually turned up a secret door, some rock that could be
		 pushed inward like a door revealing a kind of hand-cranked elevator.

			 her finger.

	 crystals.
		-It actually seemed rather friendly, and spoke Common. It wanted to sell us it's polished
		 rocks and mushrooms.

		-They'd set up shop in front of of a bunch of big, glowing crystals, shedding a bright-as-

		-We fell to discussing the area with the critters. They mentioned several things of interest:
			-We were nicer than the last one of our sort who came through, who further questioning

			 like our drow.

			 "Well, there's the. . . whatchou call it. . . big lizard thing?" one of them offered. "It
			  does something with it's eyes. . . Well, not to our kind. . . It's where we got these
			  rocks!"
			 "A basilisk?!?" Lucien growled. "Do you mean _a basilisk_?"
			 "Yes! That's the word!" the floater replied.
			 ". . . When did you last see it?" Lucien asked.
			 "Oh! Just a few moments ago, actually. . ."
	-That revelation kicked off quite the flurry of activity, with people variously throwing their
	 hands over their eyes or (unwisely) casting their eyes about, looking for the creature.
		-As I guess having seen that makes clear, I did the latter, before hurridly switching to
		 the former.
		-Not a moment too soon, either, it sounded like, as I soon heard a hissing noise, coming from
		 the direction I thought the glowing crystals were.
		-I began stumbling off in the opposite direction, looking for something to hide behind,
		 nearly tripping over Grimble in the process.
		-Finding my a suitable feeling lump of rock, I ducked behind it and began to activate my
		 precognition.
			-As I did so, I could hear a loud hum begin, coming from the direction of the crystals. . .
			-When the power took effect, it. . . was never like this before. I could catch _intense_
			 glimpses of many possible near-futures, the effect stronger than ever.
			-But, I _also_ felt the flash of memory, scenes of my home plane that were decidedly
			 unwelcome. I couldn't tell if something simply reminded me of home. . . or if something
			 more was going on in this suspiciously crystal-studded cavern.
		-Meanwhile, the sounds of battle had begun, behind the rock I leaned against.

		-He grunted in response, and then began to chant arcane syllables. Stopping the chant, he
		 then began to scream with what sounded like (feigned?) fear, yelling, "Ahhh!!! I don't think

		  I. . . don't think he's alive. . ."

		-She touched Grimble's glassy form and something. . . emerged. . . from it, a forked black
		 crystal that floated up from his chest, and then hovered above him.

		-Not heeding the warning I barely had begun to get out, Jade reached out and grabbed the

		-I could see some wisdom in that, the support of allies. . . and that I was going to be out
		 voted here.

4/15/24:
	-Jade and D'Roc began talking about how to carry Grimble, settling on D'Roc carrying the ten

		-Jade eyes indeed widened, and she began to babble a bit, mostly to herself.

		 to redirect an attack with sword. . . outward. Make a weapon, for the ship."

	-As we walked on, the enormous crystals proved a confusing reflective maze, but, despite some
	 brief uncertainty, D'Roc lead us out of it, and into some more traditionally-walled tunnels.

	 a crevasse.

		  legs or four. Or, here, a thousand. . ."
		-The party indeed stopped a bit short, casting our eyes and ears about before continuing.

		-We gathered up our various lengths of rope, passing an end of each to Maya, who flew them
		 across the cavern.

			 around a handy rock formation.

		 "Fuck no!"
		-We _all_ kept a close watch, and moved cautiously, which was a good thing, as Jade pointed

			-Weirdly, I then caught a flash of Jade falling to the ground, but only a blink later

			-Casting my eyes about, I saw magic energies fading from about Bruce's hands, presumably

	-Following D'Roc a bit further, he halted again.

	-In hushed whispers, we proposed an ambush, killing anyone but our target and, those of us with

		-A melee soon ensued a short distance ahead of me, Lucien, Jade, and D'Roc tangling with the
		 dog-things while the drow fell back, our target launching crossbow bolts and his sister

		 which should be a longer term solution than my power.

	 target, while I held tight to his brain.
		-Jade eventually offered to take over, claiming she could exercise a somewhat more subtle
		 control.
		-She chanted some Draconic syllables, and then gave me a nod.

4/29/24:
	-The enscrolled drow described to us a route back, through several hidden passages and other
	 ingeneous short cuts.
		-We took him at his (compelled) word and followed him to the surface.
		-The dark elf didn't seems to much enjoy the sunny day we emerged into, but the rest of us
		 sure did. . . and he didn't have any choice.
		-Sarge had a handy Wand of Message, and also essentially specialized in signal flares (being
		 some kind of pyromancer and all), so we had soon signaled our location to the ship and
		 got picked up.
		-Our newfound flump friends had followed us all the way to the surface and were happy to
		 join us aboard ship.
			-They were ooh-ing and ah-ing over, well, everything since we left The Underdark.
			-I wisely suggested leashing them to the ship before we got underway, lest a stray wind
			 sweep them off who knows where.
	-All aboard the ship, we headed back to Sharaar Kol.
	-A storm was blowing in, though, and soon the airship was tossing and shuddering in the winds.
		-The crew and I did what we could to keep the ship under control.
		-It was going well, until disaster, and lightning, struck one of the sails which was soon
		 alight.
		-I called out for help, shouting over the wind, "Shit's on fire! Who can conjure some water
		  or the like?"
		 "Do we have any water?" Maya shouted from the doorway to belowdecks.
		 "There's barrels in the hold!" I replied at the top of my lungs.
		-Maya soon returned with a bucket of water, splashing it all around, and was thankfully
		 followed by D'Roc carrying an entire barrel.
		-Maya took wing with the bucket, dousing part of the burning sail and then returning for
		 more water from D'Roc's bucket.
		-Her next load of water spilled uselessly into the air, though, and, D'Roc, in an effort
		 to help, hurled the barrel itself. . . which crashed through the rapidly disintegrating
		 sail.
		-"Cut the sail free!" I shouted. "We can limp back without it!"
		-The crew began to hack away at the sail's riggin and spars, with mixed success until D'Roc
		 joined with his axe, cutting easily through the spars.
		-As the burning sail fell free, I maneuvered the now-damaged ship out of the storm clouds
		 and into calmer air.
	-We had better weather for the remainder of the journey, and enough time to get some rest.
		-Before turning in, Jade made sure to do some careful maintenance on the spell holding the
		 drow in bondage.
		-After her nap, Maya emerged from her cabin with a tiny brass dragon in tow.
			-"Uh, where'd you find that, Maya?" I asked.
			 "He came to me in a dream while I was meditating," she replied.
			 "Shit. I wish more of _my_ dreams came true. . ."
			-Clearly, she's made another not-imaginary friend. Pretty on brand for her.
	-Soon, we were back in Sharaar Kol.
		-We were drawing even more stares than usual, us and our magically multiplying managerie of
		 various creatures, but particularly the drow.
		-Guards rushed to meet us, demanding an explanation.
			-"Relax, guys," I reassured them. "The king had us retrieve this prisoner for him to
			  interrogate. Jade here has him enscrolled."
		-They then offered us an escort to the king, which we happily accepted, and soon we were in
		 the king's audience chamber.
			-The flumps followed us there, ooh-ing and ah-ing over the city.
			-"Yeah, it's a solid place, guys," I said. "The dwarves know their drink!"
			-It was soon established that the flumps had no idea what booze was, and I had a mission.
		-The king was happy to see us returning successfully, and Jade began to ask about where we
		 could secure the prisoner so she could release his mind.
			-"Wait, release his mind?" I asked. "_Why_, Jade? Lets just get the answers we need
			  while he's compelled to answer!"
			-She looked rather uncomfortable at the idea, and proved unwilling, but the king was
			 fine with the matter and I didn't much care so long as we were going to get paid.
			-As such, they led him off to a cell.
		-Once in a cell, Jade released the drow's mind, leading to a sudden grimace on the prisoner's.
		 face, and we began the interrogation.
			-Lucien furnished us with copious threats, and soon we got through to our prisoner.
				-I remained less than convinced this was kinder than mind control. . .
			-The king demanded answers to why the drow was comissioning attacks on caravans in the
			 region and, after a couple of evasions, gave a name, Shadlock, claiming he'd employed
			 the drow in this matter.
			-Maya and Jade clearly recognized the name, as did the king, who was enraged.
			-The king began to call for the death of this Shadlock and the drow both, but Maya
			 counciled mercy, or at least caution, saying that the drow should be retained while
			 pursuing Shadlock, for information and testimony.
			-Maya was able to persuade the king, and the two of them fell to discussing what to do
			 to settle the region, given this Shadlock's plots.
				-The king asked first for Maya's help, and then her father's, but she pled other
				 commitments.
				-He settled on sending a cousin of his, by the wonderfully dwarven name of Lord
				 Alestone, to oversee the matter, and advise the newly minted bandit-turned-lord.
			-Maya also took a moment to introduce the king to our flump-y friends, and asked him to
			 help set them up in the city.
				-They settled on letting them hang around the local miner's school, an institution
				 dwarves apparently begin attending in childhood.
		-Taking our leave of the king, we led the flumps to the school and introduced them to some
		 of the staff there (they were at least as interested in the rocks strewn around).
			-Before daying our goodbyes, though, I insisted they join us for a celebratory drink.
			-We found a tavern and I called out the the barkeep, "These poor critters have never
			  had a proper drink! Help me fix that!"
			 "Sure! What'll they have?"
			 "Well, they sure love mushrooms. . . Got anything with mushrooms in it?"
			-The barkeep described a beer fermented in barrels covered in mushooms and I ordered
			 a round (and soon several more).
			-What we got was something like a cream of mushroom soup, with a bit of boozy bite.
			-Soon, two of the flumps were floating upside down and the third was on his third.
				-One of them brought up a new rock selling scheme: _tasty_ rocks.
				-That lit up Jade's eyes, and she began discussing the salt business with them. She
				 had apparently recruited her sales force.
					-And quite the talented one! They were brimming over with suggestions. We
					 particularly liked the idea of _colorful_ salt, and decided on blue as quite
					 striking.
				-Maya even helped them come up with a catchy jingle: https://discord.com/channels/560915739796570113/560915739796570119/1234678503945801779
		-Those of of not so lightweight that we float then fell to discussing our plan for rescuing/
		 resurrecting Grimble.
			-We pooled what I and others knew about Edric's realm, with focus on how to get there
			 (and, perhaps more importantly, how to get back).
			-Maya thought Ed might have Grimble on the layer featuring Rovert's . . . remains.
				-Ugh. Not a place I want to visit.
				-Apparently she'd heard rumors of. . . transformations, conducted there.
			-Jade and Maya both pushed the idea of seeking the protection of some other god, to
			 protect us from Edric.
				-I was decidedly leery of that prospect, though came closest to comfort with Maya's
				 framing of it as _commerce_: doing a favor or the like for some god in return for
				 their protection against Edric.
				-The notion of seeking out other members of The Brotherhood came up, but I was
				 almost as deeply against that as just kowtowing to Edric. After all, their his
				 allies, and probably more inclined to help him than us.
				-The fact that gnomes have a god was also brought up and, knowing Grimble's people,
				 that sounded a bit more attractive to me. We resolved to talk with Grimble's kin,
				 back aboard the ship.
			-We also talked a lot about options for getting to Edric's realm.
				-Jade can make Planeshift scrolls, but Grimble would put us over the headcount
				 limit and each casting risks dumping us some random distance away from our target.
					-Maya had apparently heard of an extra-planar _copy_ of Xl-Jarak, used as a
					 meeting place by The Brotherhood, something we could use to our advantage with
					 planeshift.
						-I actually visited there as a kid, with my creche!
						-It was no bigger than the fortress, and thus hard to get lost in with
						 Planeshift, but was linked to all the planes of The Brotherhood.
						-Maya even claimed that the key to Edric's plane would _also_ let us
						 Planeshift there!
				-There are also portals, famously the one at Xl-Jarak where I myself arrived on The
				 Material Plane.

5/24/24:
	-Sitting in the tavern, one flump upright and two floating upside down, we continued discussing
	 our plan to get Grimble back (and my traumatic childhood).
		-Jade zoned out for a bit, doing a bit of crystal-fueled crafting.
		-We debated a lot of ideas for leverage, with Edric or even other gods.
			-Gods came up a bunch.
				-We might be able to seek the help of Garl Glittergold. Grimble wasn't really a
				 worshipper, but he sure was an excellent _gnome_ nonetheless: a trickster and
				 master of illusions.
				-Sarge reminded us that I'd mentioned a late companion, Isaias, a cleric of Shawn,
				 who may have been a cleric of Enilias disguised.
					-That certainly speaks to some turmoil, now or when this is revealed, in The
					 Brotherhood, and maybe the possibility of seeking alliances there.
					-It was also on my list of "report back" material.
					-Jade chimed in, pointing out that it was on Isaias's body that we found her
					 orb, a thing he'd never mentioned before his death.
			-I spoke more about the kind of things Edric wants, which it's ostensibly my job to
			 find, but also about how what he almost certainly wants from this is me: information
			 about me and my capabilities, and doubtlessly to put me to some kind of test.
		-In service of exploring. . . services (?) from Garl Glittergold, we decided we should talk
		 talk with Grimble's kin about the subject.
			-"Lets go fetch them. They could probably use a stiff drink, after the news about
			  Grimble. . . Who can run there fastest?" I asked.
			-Lucien raised his hand, so I said to him, "Great! I'll race you there! I'll even give
			 you a head start! You take off and I'll follow when I finish this drink. . ."
				-I ordered another, after he left, and before finishing the one I had.
	-After some further discussion of our plans here, we noticed it had been quite a while that
	 Lucien had been gone. . . even if he strolled up to the docks.
		-We called for the check and were getting ready to follow him when he burst into the bar,
		 hand on his sword hilt.
		-Apparently there'd been yet _another_ kidnapping of my friends: my entire crew.
		-Lucien's devil-brother, Sangravos, was apparently waiting for him, and had taken my crew
		 hostage.
		-Apparently he wanted our help ingratiating himself with the king of Sharaar Kol.
			-A mass kidnapping is a funny way to get that. . .
			-I told him as much, claiming that I certainly can't convince the king to trust him 
			 while something like this is between us. I'm not a good liar. . .
				-He had to concede _both_ points.
		-Fortunately, Maya charmed (magically and regularly both, I think) the pants of off him
		 (thankfully not literally).
			-She convinced him that we could _never_ sell the king on such a thing while we were
			 frantically trying to rescue a friend, and now more friends. If he were to release
			 the crew and come back in a day. . .
			-He couldn't resist her and assented. He waved his hand, leading to some stirring in
			 the hold, and then teleported away.
		-Soon, the crew was emerging from below decks, all talking over one another about how a
		 devil tied them up.
	-With the crew restored to us, we took the opportunity to ask Grimble's kin about Garl
	 Glittergold.
		-"Dimble, Bimble, and Timble, what do you guys know about Garl Glittergold?"
		-They seemed to be about as religious as Grimble, and could really only speak about folksy
		 generalities, saying stuff like, "Uh. . . Well, he loves tricks. Oh! And he likes when
		 little gnomes clean their rooms!"
		 "It's alright guys," I told them. "I slept through religion class too. . ."
		 "You had religion classes?" D'Roc asked.
		 "I grew up in a place directly, and rigidly, run by the god who made me! Of course there
		  were religion classes. . ."
		-Timble _did_ volunteer that we could consult with a cleric of Glittergold.
			-Consulting with _him_, and the rest of his resident kin, we determined the location of
			 the gnome burrow nearest to Sharaar Kol, which he assured us would have one.
	-With a trip to visit some gnomes in mind, we went off in search of a shipwright, to fix our
	 burned and severed sail.
		-Forunately, the airdocks was unsurprisingly the place to find one, and we quickly made our
		 way inside such an establishment, Edgar's.
		-We were greeted warmly by it's owner, proprietor, and namesake, who was happy to do the
		 work, but who, upon hearing about our haste, regrettably informed us that he was closing
		 up for the night and that his employees were already off at a tavern.
			-We offered him additional money for speedy work, but he doubted he could convice his
			 workers to return this evening.
		-Maya, though, once more turned on her charm.
			-Just the regular kind, I think, given the less abrupt and more plausible effect it had
			 on him.
		-That had quite the impact, with Edgar soon enamored with her, saying that he'd
		 set about the work immediately, and work all through the night! He frantically gathered
		 up some tools and then ran out the door to our nearby ship.
		-He lept the gap between dock and ship, heedless of the great plunge between, and began to
		 assess the damage.
			-That rather alarmed Maya.
	-We shouted to the dwarf, asking where his crew could be found, so that we could try our own
	 luck at convincing them to come back to work. We then rushed off to that bar, though Maya
	 opted to stay back and keep an eye on Edgar, to catch him should he fall.
		-Inside the bar, we found a rowdy group of dwarves dressed in identical work uniforms and
		 deep into the booze _flights_ strewn about on the table before them.
		-We sat down with them and I called for another round of the same flights, for all of us,
		 making a proper introduction.
		-Confirming they worked for Edgar, we started to raise the issue of our damaged
		 sail, but were met with laughter as one said, "You should talk to the boss about that. . ."
		 "I did! I replied. "He was doubting you guys could do it. . ."
		 "Well, another replied, we are five rounds deep. . ."
		 "Exactly!" I said, cutting him off. "That's a mere appetizer to dwarves! He seemed to doubt
		  your fortitude. . . But, seeing you lot, I sure don't! Now, look, guys, I hate to delay
		  you reaching the main course, but we are willing to pay for the rush job. . ."
		-We were soon on the way back to the ship, with at least two of the dwarves having trouble
		 walking in a straight line.
		-As we reached the ship, the grinning Edgar told his employees he's joining our
		 crew, and I was of course on board, he being a skilled shipwright.
			-"Cedgar, my son, you're in charge now! You'll just have to add a letter on the sign. . ."
		-The crew then joined their boss in the work.
		-One dwarf, on the drunker end of the crowd, almost immediately fell to his seemingly certain
		 death, but Maya took (magic) wing, swooping down to grab him, and tossed a line back up to
		 D'Roc who hauled the two of them back up.
			-Gazing at D'Roc, that clumsy dwarf muttered, "You know, your remind me of something. . ."
			-The two of them, soon joined by Maya and Jade, discussed a place that D'Roc indeed
			 believed sounded like his long lost home, dwarven legends apparently telling of such a
			 maze.
				-Maya and Jade discussed some arcane quirk of cosmology where mazes are apparently
				 a part of the early formation of a plane.
	-With the repairs underway, our comrades and I spent the time discussing how to deal with the
	 devil.
		-I suggested murder, and Lucien enthusiastically agreed. . .which was good. Some people do
		 take offense to proposals to murder their siblings. . .
		-Jade volunteered that she could create a binding circle, for trapping outsiders, which
		 certainly interested us for the current problem!
			-To set that up, we picked the antechamber to the captain's quarters, and Jade began
			 painstakingly creating an elaborate diagram on the floor in powdered silver.
			-Jade thought she could summon him and bind him in the circle.
			-Lucien even volunteered his blood, the blood of our target's kin, and Jade agreed that
			 she could make use of that to strengthen the ward, solomnly accepting a cup full of his
			 donation.
			-As she worked, Jade warned all of us, "Breaking the circle will free him, as will
			 hostile actions towards him."
				-We conveyed that message to the crew too, telling them to stay out of the room,
				 under any and all circumstances.
	-Jade then commenced the summoning ritual.
		-Soon, the devil faded into view before us, and he greeted Maya warmly.
		-Through gritted teeth, and minding the warning about "hostile actions", Lucien growled,
		 "Nice to see you, brother. So. . . good, to have you back on The Material Plane. . ."
		 "Ah, Maya! I see you civilized him," the demon goaded Lucien. "He's a regular lap dog these
		  days!"
		-Lucien was instantly enraged, and stepped towards the circle.
		-Jade then grabbed his arm, talking to him in low quiet tones, and pulled him towards my
		 bedchamber.
			-I chimed in, "Yeah. . . Play it cool. No need to get _hostile_. . . yet."
		-That left me to play for time with the devil.
			-We talked of booze, The Material, and of how surprisingly similar our homes were.
				-"Huh. Awful, layers, and run by tyrannical jerks. That _does_ sound familiar. . ."
			-He could read a surprising amount about me, though whether is was simple sight, magic,
			 or foreknowledge, and apparently saw in that an opportunity.
				-"Where you come from. . . psionics are common, are they not? You yourself are
				  clearly so empowered. These jerks you speak of. . . I could offer you what every
				  captain dreams of: a treasure map. And one that leads to an artifact that would
				  shield your mind. . ."
				 ". . . Uh. . . Tell me more. . ."
				 "All you would need to do is release me. . ."
			-Jade, though, burst back into the room with a still fuming Lucien.
			-"Fred," she said. "We're going to leave him here for now. . . We need to further
			  discuss how we're going to. . . deal with our guest."
		-We headed out into the hall and down into the other end of the ship. There, discussed our
		 options.
			-Jade had apparently tried something involving a "Spectral Hand" while she was shut in
			 the bedroom, but without luck.
			-She thought she could try again until it worked, given enough time, maybe a week. . .
			-That isn't really time we have right now, but she said she'd be able to compell a
			 service from him, with these arcane tricks, and maybe some negotiation coaching from me.
			-That prompted it's own debate, but one of the most attractive options was a _dual_,
			 with Lucien, Lucien being confident he could take his brother if we set the terms such
			 that he could quickly close and stay close.
