5/29/24:
	-Jade apparently had more curses up her sleeve, and plenty of time left on her magic binding,
	 so she requested another day to prepare something more, and we eventually assented.
		-"I mean, who knows what's happening to poor Grimble. . . wherever he is?" I complained.
		 "Grimble? He's on the ship!" Bram replied.
		 "Well, _crystal_ Grimble is. . ." I clarified, "But not his soul or whatever."
	-The next morning, Jade's preparations in place, she cursed him still further, from the other
	 room using various magic implements.
	-We then opened up the door to our unpleasantly occupied dining chamber, to reveal a glaring
	 and impatient devil.
		-Maya gave us all a little speech, talking to us about how great we were, and to the devil
		 about an honorable confrontation.
		-Indeed, we then proceeded to negotiate the terms of a duel between Lucien and his brother,
		 which both assented to.
			-I sent one of my gnomish crewmen, Timble, off to grab some snacks, for us in the
			 the audience.
		-The duel itself was almost anticlimactic. Lucien breached the circle with his toe and then,
		 almost before his brother could even brace himself, Lucien drew his blade and slashed the
		 devil in one smooth motion, then finished his reeling sibling with another as he brought
		 the blade, glowing with holy energies, back down.
			-Those energies probably have a lot to do with why the devil basically exploded.
			-I also had to call Timble back, on account of the brevity of the duel, and ask him to
			 fetch some rags instead.
	-That left the room _drenched_ in blood.
		-In fact, Lucien was really _staring_ at his handiwork. Even more strangely, he was soon
		 joined in that by Jade, who staring at blood was a bit less in character for.
		-That mystery was soon explained, though. They fell to discussing the nature of the planes,
		 and bandied about terms like "hemospicy", and eventually clued the rest of us in.
			-Apparently, something about a devil's passage between planes marks it, and they
			 believed they could divine where in The Hells the devil departed from, based on the
			 patterns formed from his bloody demise.
			-Jade then set to recording the splatters _on Lucien_, before the two set to arguing
			 about the patterns in the gore there and elsewhere, and their meanings.
			-They came to the conclusion that he'd left from the seventh level of The Nine Hells,
			 Maladomini, a place ruled by the infernal prince Baalzebul.
	-Well, with that bloody matter settled, we made the ship ready to depart and then sought out
 	 the gnome town my crew had told me about.
		-In the course of the trip from Sharaar Kol, we passed above the Shieldwall Mountains.
		-A short way past the mountains foothils, the air elementals grew restive. I could feel it
		 in the ships handling.
		-Seeking them out below decks, there had been a subtle change in their hue, a grayer tone.
		-Asking them what was wrong, they gave me only vague answers, about a "change in the wind".
		-They seemed to have little idea of what they were feeling themselves, but had instead
		 some instinctive connection to their element.
		-I warned everyone aboard to keep an eye out, and it was a short while later that Bruce
		 called out from the crow's nest (_bat's_ nest?).
		-He had sighted some kind of. . . floating platform? Even with my attention called to it,
		 I could barely make it out in the dark clouds. There was definitely _something_ there,
		 though.
		-We elected to give it a wide berth, and spent a tense dozen minutes on alert while we
		 passed.
		-Pass we did, though, and soon we were clear of the mountains, with the elementals back to
		 normal a short while later.
	-Soon thereafter, we were flying above The Shining Valley.
		-We sighted an elaborate, heavily mechanized dock at one end of the valley, one which my
		 crewman Himble confirmed was operated by the gnomes (and which he proceeded to go on at
		 length about it's many fine mechanical marvels).
		-We brought the ship into a berth on the airdock, and soon I was chatting with the
		 dockmaster.
		-After collecting his fee for the berth, he was _at least_ as enthusiastic about his docks.
		-After some pleasantries, I was soon steering him toward Jade, who was all too happy to
		 talk with him at length about mechanisms, particularly his pride and joy, the modulated
		 sprocket, a. . . thing he'd apparently invented.
			-I _did_ catch the dockmaster mentioning to Jade the many fine and exotic materials
			 available in this settlement, a thing she (and I, though her) might love to take
			 advantage of.
		-Eventually she brought the conversation back around to our need for a priest, and asked
		 for directions.
			-Apparently that was something of a faux pas. He informed us that only gnomes were
			 supposed to know the location of Garl Glittergold's temple.
			-After some wheedling on Maya's part, though, he gave in and revealed that the temple
			 was beneath the settlement.
			-However, to get in, there was an obstacle: admittance to the temple require that we
			 somehow prank one of it's secret guardians. No one knows who they are, but impressing
			 them in this way is what's required to earn their approval, and entry into the temple.
		-Coming up with an impressive prank stumped us for some time. . . so I suggested a bar.
			-Somewhere between my fourth and eighth whiskey, we settled on a scheme, mostly built
			 on a joke Maya suggested: asking for a priest to help my pony. . . because he's a
			 little horse.
			-That soon ballooned into a dragon battle and all sorts of (planned) chaos.
		-It required some spell preparation on Jade and Bruce's parts, though so we turned in for
		 the evening with a plan to execute our prank over the lunch hour tomorrow.
	-The next morning, some miserable gnomish contraption woke me. An "alarm clock" is what the
	 inn's proprietor named it, when I came down and complained.
	-Around lunchtime, we headed to a small public square, outside a popular restaurant.
		-While Jade conjured a pony, I made sure everyone knew their parts in the plan.
		-I then ran at the restaurant, waving my hands over my head, yelling, "Run for your lives!
		 The dragon! The beast! It's here!"
		-D'Roc and the pony were fast on my heels, with, shortly behind them, Maya's tiny dragon
		 and Lucien.
			-The last was cackling evilly in a way that played up his devilish heritage.
			-Sarge also contributed some gouts of flames for the the dragon, bursting in the air
			 overhead.
		-D'Roc picked up the pony and ran past me, but I halted, and shouted, "I'll scare them off!"
		-I then let out the cutest, _least_ intimidating roar I could manage, my best impression of
		 a squeaky kitten, which nonetheless caused Lucien to flee, though without deterring the
		 dragon.
		-Unfortunately, I was not the only one responding to the "attack".
			-Some form of automaton emerged from a nearby alleyway.
			-In an ominous mechanical voice, it demanded calm, and then began encasing nearby
			 gnomes in some kind of domes of force.
		-D'Roc then set the pony down and turned to face the dragon, drawing his axe.
		-They had a quick mock battle and then "struck down" the dragon, which began spurting comical
		 gouts of what I would swear was wine. . . or perhaps it's underage cousin, grape juice.
		-The dragon's "demise" thankfully quieted the construct.
		-I then ran to "my" poney and screamed, adding, "My pony! The dragon got her! I need a
		 priest!"
		-I kept repeating that last bit until I noticed a gnome waving and yelling, from beneath
		 one of the domes.
		-"I'm the priest!" he yelled as I got closer. "But I'm stuck!"
		-D'Roc then shattered the dome with his axe, and the priest stood up as it's shards
		 disintegrated around him.
		-"What's wrong with your pony?" he asked me.
		 "Oh! He's a little horse. . ." I replied, as the horse gave forth Jade's (terrible) singing
		 voice.
	-The gnomish priest groaned loudly, saying, "I see what this is. Fine. . ."
		-He then drew a door with his finger in the dirt of the square beneath him.
		-Grasping it's "knob", he pulled the apparently realer than it looked door open, revealing
		 a stair going downward into the earth.
		-The party gathered around and then descended, emerging into a carnival scene. . .


6/10/24:
	-The temple was filled with gnomes, conjuring illusions, practicing acrobatics, and telling
	 jokes, resulting in the carnival atmosphere.
		-There were though also artificers and engineers, practicing _their_ talents and trades to,
		 dedicating the works to their god.
		-I cast my eyes looking for someone in charge, ring master or high priest either, but it was
		 Maya who first spotted and pointed out that a considerable amount of what we were witnessing,
		 gnomes, furnishings, and even space, were in fact illusions covering a smaller temple and
		 somewhat less worshipers.
		-She also said that she felt there were two factions or schools in the temple, split along
		 the lines of their talents: jokers and artisans.
		-Well, the jokers are clearly Grimble's and my people, and I said as much, suggesting we
		 seek help there.
		-We followed the call of a carnival barker of sorts, which led us to an illusory play of
		 sorts, one telling some tale of a split between gnomes and kobolds.
			-There were also some bits about an eclipse and other astronomical phenomena.
			-I didn't really follow that, though. . . maybe because where I come from doesn't have
			 a sky.
		-We also observed a variety of other displays, shows, and shrines.
			-Another series of illusions showed Garl Glittergold pranking other gods.
				-The pranks were good natured, save where kobolds were concerned.
			-There was also a lavish statue of a gnome with gemstone eyes.
		-Eventually Maya pointed out a particularly unobtrusive gnome, one seemingly repeating lines
		 to himself in one corner.
			-"In this place where little is what it seems, the leader won't be flashy and obvious,"
			 she added.
			-Shrugging in response, I approached the gnome and asked, "What are you working on? Need
			 a stand-in for whatever you're practicing?" I asked.
			 "The tree. . ." he said, "Should it disappear or turn into a T-Rex?"
			 "Uh. . ."
			 "Oh, sorry! You need the context. . ." the gnome added. "I need to impart a moral
			  lesson. Someone stole sacred jewelry, a very grave crime."
			 "What's a T-Rex?" Jade broke in.
			 "Ah, it's a, well, a kind of lizard. . . a very large one," the priest explained.
			 "Oh! Like a dragon?" Maya asked.
			 "Uh, yeah, kind of! But with really short arms. . " the priest replied.
			 "Ah. I think something like that killed a buddy of mine. . ." I said, killing the mood
			 a little bit.
			 "I'm sorry. . ." the priest said. "What happened?"
			 "Well," I explained, "We _did_ learn a moral lesson, one about rushing in without a
			  plan. . ."
				-Adding that last bit, I glared briefly at Maya.
			 "But!" I continued, perking up. "_That's_ why I vote T-Rex. They teach a _mean_ lesson."
			-I then took the opportuninty to steer the conversation around to our own agenda, saying,
			 "Actually, we've need to teach something of a moral lesson of our own. . ."
			-I then told him about my lost friend, Grimble: how he was a paragon of gnomishness,
			 with his great talent for illusions and great sense of humor, and the story of Grimble's
			 mistreatment by Edric.
			-The priest knew of Edric for his industrial pursuits, and generally respected him for
			 them.
			-"The problem is," I explained, "He treats _people_ like _things_. . . and doesn't
			  hesitate to make things out of them."
			-He soon saw the issue, and agreed it was a grave misdeed by someone who clearly needs
			 to lighten up.
			-Seeing the nobility of our cause, and the stick up Ed's ass, he agreed to offer us aid.
			-In particular, he handed us each a small, fragile-seeming gemstone, explaining that, if
			 we break them against a creature, the creature will disappear and be replaced with an
			 illusory double.
				-A handy thing, given Edric's unpleasant interest in yours truely.
				-Bruce even handed his to me, saying his vow of poverty forbids his use of such
				 things.
			-Jade also asked the priest, "What else do you know of The Brotherhood?"
				-He mentioned, in reply, rumors of some kind of falling out, with the various gods
				 of The Brotherhood retreating to their own realms and agendas. "Their shared realm
				 is. . . sort of in disrepair?" he added.
				-He also said that Nikisi had pissed off Myrkul, but that the church of Garl
				 Glittergold actually regarded Enelias rather fondly, for his talents for trickery.
				-The priest also shared that Shawn's adventuring academy is going strong, but
				 concerns itself with the broader cosmic balance more than the rest of The
				 Brotherhood.
				-Beyond the gods, he also mentioned an artificer that had been associated with The
				 Brotherhood, one "2d6", who it's said left enchanted items behind hoping that one
				 day someone would take them up to help The Brotherhood.
					-Jade started fidgeting a bit at that.
					-"Do you think he's still around?" she asked the gnome.
					 "Don't see why not, given that he's a warforged."
			-Given that the priest clearly knew a lot about The Brotherhood, I also asked him about
			 the statue of a gnome with (alarming, to me) crystal eyes.
				-"That's Garl Glittergold himself!" the gnome explained. "It's said that every
				  thousand years or so he even inhabits the statue. Gets up to all sorts of things!"
	-That matter settled, we adjourned to a tavern and returned to discussing our planned approach
	 to The Brotherhood.
		-We talked a bit about The Brotherhood's shared realm, their otherworldly fortress of
		 Xl-Jarak.
		-Jade also brought up the card game she's been dreaming of for some time, wondering if
		 Edric would be interested in such things.
			-It actually sounded like _very_ much his kind of thing, and I told Jade as much.
			-She rapidly got excited, talking quickly about properties, odds, and the appeal of her
			 cards-and-illusions game.
			-I was eventually able to get a word in edgewise, and cautioned her, saying, "Remember
			 what this is really about, Jade: we need to get Grimble back. . . not find you an
			 investor."
			-She nodded solomnly, in response.
			-Well, it's at least another bargaining chip. . .
		-Sarge also raised aid from others of The Brotherhood, a thing I'm more amenable to than I
		 was before we learned The Brotherhood wasn't exactly in the perfect harmony the teachers
		 described to me back in the creche.
			-Jade ran with that too, talking of where she might be able to find more keys for her
			 orb.
			-She also suggested that she and Maya could both reach out, via their magic books, to
			 their people in Sasserine, asking them to (discretely) inquire with any churches of
			 the gods of The Brotherhood in Sasserine, about their gods' interests and agendas.
				-They indeed spent some time scribbling to their correspondents, and conferring
				 with one another about what instructions to give.
		-Jade also continued to have an unhealthy interest in her orbs and the keys that fit within
		 it. She kept insisting that more keys. . . would somehow help, but couldn't seem to say
		 exactly what they would do.
			-Drawing on the gnome priest's story about 2d6, and some claims of a "harmonious"
			 purpose for the artifact, Jade made the case for her study of it. . . Well, she figured
			 that harmony can't be bad, right?
			-I was quick to correct her, "It's for the harmony _of The Brotherhood_! That's not what
			 _we_ want. We're sitting here debating if we can use divisions in The Brotherhood to
			 our advantage here. . ."
			-She did insist, though, that the orb and it's purpose might be something Edric would
			 be willing to bargain for. Which, fair enough.


8/5/24:
	-We talked a few last details over, but even I had run out of excuses to avoid going home.
		-The only additional thing we prepared was another plane shift scroll, crafted by Jade as
		 we were worried that bringing Grimble back with us would push us over the limit of the
		 spell.
	-So, we finally performed the plane shift, all of us grasping hands in a circle as Jade recited
	 the incantation from the scroll, to take us to the (far smaller) demiplane on which The
	 Brotherhood had constructed it's planar nexus, and Xl-Jarak clone.
	-The world shifted and twisted and, as it melted back into intelligible shapes, we found ourselves
	 standing before a forboding fortress: all sharp angles and made from a black metal.
		-"Ugh," I said. "That did not play nice with the red wine I had for breakfast. . . Next
		  time, I'm sticking to white before plane shifting."
		-Forboding though it was, it was hardly devoid of life: there were various groups of all
		 sorts of creatures, scattered across it's ramparts and battlements.
		-I approached a nearby group of halfling-sized rat people, saying, "Hello, there my fuzzy
		  friend! Do you think you could help us with some directions!
			-He was well-mannered and helpful both, and more than happy to show us around.
			-I explained to him that I was from Edric's Enlightened Spheres, and looking to head
			 home, but he was also very proud of the copy-fort, eagerly pointing out various
			 landmarks.
				-He was a big fan of Shawn's adventuring academy, suggesting we consider classes
				 there, and pointing it out to us.
				-He also showed us the tavern, which, were Grimble's fate less urgent, _I_ would be
				 a very big fan of.
					-Actually, D'Roc was quite interested too, after our ratman guide mentioned Dog.
					-Apparently, some of the trophies on the wall were _his_, brought back from the
					 god's hunting grounds.
					-D'Roc was very interested in reaching his god's promised land, and, indeed, the
					 ratman explained they could be reached from here, _if_ the petitioner proved
					 himself a worthy hunter (at which he gestured to some of the trophies).
						-There was even a bounty board of sorts: posted reports of great beasts,
						 whose slaying would bring the favor of Dog.
						-Most prominent among them was a Nightmare, a black horse wreathed in flames
						 that had been sighted in the frontier nation of Q'barra, 
				-He also showed us a space he referred to as the throne room, but said it was mostly
				 used to host a regular market, though we'd come on the wrong day.
			-Intriguing as all that was, I had to press the matter of my route. . . home.
			-"Oh!" he said. "If you have the key, there's a portal you can activate with it, in the
			  throne room. Or. . . there are open portals in the basement, but it's been infested
			  for a millennia."
			 "There rats down there?" D'Roc asked, insensitively.
				-I, standing behind the ratman, waved my hands, trying to mime that D'Roc should
				 knock it off, and pointing at our guide.
			 "Hmph. . . No. Undead," he replied.
			-Another of his kind then called out, waving to him, saying, "Beauregard!"
			 "Oh! That's my wife," our guide explained. "Well, best of luck to you all! Coming, my
			  dear!"
			-"Well, Jade. . . Do we have the right key?" I asked.
				-She nodded, and got to fishing about in her orb.
				-Withdrawing a black adamantine one, Jade wandered to the far end of the throne room
				 and, indeed finding a keyhole on the wall opposite the main entrance, she inserted
				 and turned the key.
				-That transformed the wall into a rippling portal, and we all stepped through.
	-This time, we found ourselves in a desert scattered with wreckage: The Borderlands.
		-"D'Roc, we need to find a hole, to descend to a lower layer. There's probably a lot of
		  traffic in and out so. . . see any tracks?"
		-He nodded and got to looking.
		-Something caught his eye near the rusty hulk of some enormous. . . airship, maybe?
			-It was half embedded in the sand in any case.
			-He followed some trail over to a great rent in the old hulk.
			-As he approached the dark opening, though, he halted, shaking his head as if to clear
			 it.
			-"Uh, D'Roc?" I called out. "Don't go listening to any voices!"
			-He babbled something about a "chittering". . . and soon we could hear it too.
		-The source was soon revealed, as a band of thri-kreen appeared from the rent in the wreck,
		 some of them aboard a strange, rumbling machine.
			-They had their weapons at the ready and Sarge was already reaching for his spell
			 component pouch, but I tried to de-escelate things.
			-Raising my hands away from my swordbelt, I called out, to bug and buddy both, "Be cool!
			  We're here because Edric called for us. You don't want to piss off _god_ do you?"
			-The thri-kreen seemed to follow at least _some_ Common, as they took a step or two back,
			 lowering their weapons.
			-We began some linguistically-impaired negotiation, mostly consisting of Maya and I
			 dancing.
			-Dance proved to be a rather universal language, and Maya, in particular, seemed to get
			 across that. . . I was the son of god and needed to go see my father.
			-Well, it got the job done, as one of them began to draw a map in the sand.
			-It indeed featured a hole, but also. . . what I thought, at first, was a thri-kreen,
			 but which the one drawing seemed to be taking pains to make. . . ant-like?
				-In any event, it was depicted between us and the hole.
			-That sparked a recollection from my childhood. In one of the rare, exciting bits of
			 creche classes that actually held my attention, I rembered learning about the thri-kreen
			 that roved The Borderlands _and their formian rivals_.
			-Well, grasping the problem, I proposed a solution: I danced forward, recoiled from the
			 drawing of the ant man, and then danced back forward and stomped the ant man.
			-The thri-kreen seemed to take my meaning, excitedly chittering amongst themselves before
			 one of the ones on the strange machine made a clear "hop on" gesture, which we happily
			 obliged.
	-We rode the bug men's strange sand ship quite a ways through the desert until it seemed to run
	 (more?) aground, the sands having grown rockier.
		-The Thri-kreen managed to indicate to us that we should now get out and walk, gesturing to
		 a rocky ridge that was visible in the distance.
		-Some of the insect band also gestured back and forth between the ridge and their weapons,
		 and it was clear to me they meant to fight alongside us.
	-We approached the rocky ridge and could soon see that portions of the stone had been worked
	 into a kind of fortress, with taller constructions inside.
		-We discussed scouting the place in some way, and eventually settled on the three of us that
		 could fly taking a look from above.
		-When they glided back down, they reported a bustling hive of activity, with numerous antmen
		 digging away at the rock, overseen by larger members of their race.
		-They also mentioned other, very different insects, possessed of wings, up on the ridge.
			-They were much larger, perhaps 10' long.
			-Bruce termed them "spider-eaters", and said one of them was doing just that, chowing
			 down on a giant spider.
		-We debated our options at length and settled on. . . another frontal assault, like the one
		 that killed my last bug buddy.
			-But, this time, we would send _summoned creatures_ in first, Jade having volunteered
			 the newly learned ability to summon giants.
	-We crept forward to the opening in the ridge that clearly served as a front gate to the
	 fortress and, once we were 20 or so feet away, Jade barked some arcane symbols, summoning a
	 pair of stone giants that then charged forward through the gap.
		-They were met by some of the larger formians, the ones that had been directing the workers.
		-One stared intently at one of the giants, in a way that felt awfully familiar to me, but
		 the giant appeared unphased.
		-D'Roc loosed some arrows at one of the ant people, to no avail as the shot went wide.
		-Far more effective was boulder one of the giants grabbed and hurled at the formian
		 taskmaster, which cracked it's exoskeleton horribly, letting flow a disgusting goo, though
		 the formian kept his feet.
		-Our thri-kreen allies then lept (literally) into the fray, as the formians formed up into
		 organized ranks and things devolved into a general melee.
		-I also began to feel an ominous rumbling, coming from the earth beneath me. . .
		-I took a shot with my bow at some kind of rock monster that emerged from one of the
		 buildings, and then darted behind a rock to use it for cover.
		-Moments later, another (or the same?) rock monster emerged from the sand near my rocky
		 cover, casting about it's eyeless face, clearly looking for me, but to no avail.
		-I stabbed it with my rapier, which merely scratched it's rocky carapace, and I tumbled
		 backwards out of it's reach.
		-The rumbling reached it's crescendo, then, as a huge rock monster emerged from the sand
		 just inside the gate and began smashing our thri-kreen allies.
			-Why always my bug buddies?!?
		-I tried to lock the huge rock man's mind, to prevent further bug smashing, but it managed
		 to resist me.
		-Thankfully, it couldn't resist D'Roc's axe, with which he cleaved it in twain.
		-As the rock monster crumbled, so to did the earth beneath him, eventually forming a hole
		 15' across, through the layer.
	-The party and I dashed towards the hole and dived in.
		-I gave a wave to our remaining bug buddies as I did so. They were now driving the remaining,
		 demoralized formians back into a retreat.
		-As we fell through the hole, the still shifting sides of the hole expelled numerous
		 gemstones, which we grasped at greedily as the tumbled in the air around us.
		-The gravity (and stomach) flip that I knew was coming seemed to quite bother the others
		 and it was the first thing they brought up when we were flung out on the topside of the
		 next layer, rather than our shiny windfall.
			-"Why is it _like_ that?!?" Jade asked.
			 "Eh, you get used to it. Plus, the elans here often don't bother eating, so it probably
			  doesn't hit them as hard," I explained.
		-We then fell to sorting through the gems, and I found I'd managed to snag the most precious
		 of them, a blue star sapphire.
			-"I got the best one!" I exclaimed. "Hey. I caught a _star_! You all saw it!"

8/19/24:
	-This new layer featured more industrial scenery: titanic metal structures and great machines.
	-There was, however, rather little activity. We didn't see any people about, and most of the
	 machinery was idle.
	-_Most_, but not all. Some short distance away, we could hear the hiss of steam coming from a
	 clanking conveyor belt that kept starting and then haulting.
		-We walked that way, following what we hoped were signs of life.
		-Approaching the machinery, we could see scorched spots on the belt, outlining, in each
		 case, a pair of footprints?
		-There were also more literal signs, ones warning about wearing safety helmets, to avoid. . .
		 implantation?
	-As we followed the stalled belt onward, the are got progressively. . . slimier, a wet green-ish
	 muck covering any and, soon, most surfaces
		-Maya spotted it _moving_.
		-"Oh, I think I remember what this is. . ." I said. "It's my great, great, great, great. . .
		  you get the idea, uncle. He had the same inborn psionics as I do, and Edric tried to turn
		  him into an elan. This was the thing that resulted. . . They say it still shows evidence
		  of _thinking_. . ."
		-I bent to scrape some of it off my boot, and got quite a bit more than evidence: it began
		 _talking_.
		-"Remember what I said about listening to voices!" I shouted to the rest.
		-The voice in my head, though, which the others seemed to also hear as soon as they touched
		 the slime, was staying instead, "Come to the center. . ."
		-I reacted by backing away slowly.
		-"Don't go!" it "said". "I'm Rovert. Who are you?"
		 "Ah. . . Uh, I'm Fred."
		 "You're Fred! Oh! It's good to meet you," the slime "said".
		 "You've heard of me?"
		 "You're the new PR guy that was supposed to be coming," it explained.
		 "Uh. . . "
		 "You know, spread the message to the Material Plane and all that! Recruit followers."
		 "Ohhh. Not a resident position, then. Well. . . do you know know who I need to talk to
		  about that?"
		 "Well, there's a tribe of kobolds?"
		 "Are they. . . like, HR, then?"
		 "Kind of! They're a bit less. . . changed, then a lot of Edric's thralls."
		-Maya then broke in asking, "Is that why you're slime?"
		 "Well, that was the result of an experiment," the slime said. "Someone pulled the wrong
		  lever. Then there was slime everywhere. . . and I _was_ the slime. It was my penance."
		 "Wait," I then said, "It was just a mistake?"
		 "Well," the voice-of-the-slime replied, "Edric said it was a cautionary tale. If you fail,
		  you're slime."
		 "Look," it continued, "Can you do me a favor? Scoop up a ball of the slime and bring it to
		  Edric. I'd really like to talk to Edric, and ask him if my penance is done."
		 "Uh. . . Jade?" I asked. "Go ahead and scoop that up. . . She's my go-to for magical stuff
		  that. . . I don't want to touch."
		-We briefly debated containers, and it turned out Jade had a rum bottle.
		 "Rum!" Rovert exclaimed. "I remember rum. . ."
		 "Can you still. . . drink rum?" Maya asked.
		 "I can feed on all _kinds_ of things these days," it replied.
		-Well, I grabbed the bottle from Jade, took a swig from it, and poured the rest into the
		 slime.
		-It seemed to appreciate the rum, making approving "noises", and Jade scooped some into the
		 emptied bottle I handed back to her.
		-"So, where to with this, Rov?" I asked.
		 "The nearest column is over there," it replied, illustrating it's point by forming a vague
		  psuedopod from the slime in the jar, pointing at a metal structure reaching all the way
		  up to the surface above us. ". . .but you'll have to get past the rest of me."
		 "Uh, what?"
		-It went on to explain that it's not so. . . unified, as once it was, and it doesn't all
		 agree with itself. We'd need to confront some dissenting opinions at the column.
	-Well, we walked over to the column.
		-There, we found the column's interior was heavily coated in slime.
		-As we approached the mass of slime, many mouths formed on it, all gibbering a discordant
		 cacophony of competing voices.
		-It. . . was almost like the chatter. . . back in school. . . I'd struggled to ignore that
		 too.
		-Then, I _was_ back in school. I'd forgotten my homework. . .
		-"No more homework. . ." I protested, futily, over and over again.
	-Eventually, I realized most of the babbling I could still hear was me. . . and that I could
	 also hear. . . singing?
		-As I regained my sense, I found Maya had coaxed the mouths into a chorus.
			-A bit flat, but better than the babbling!
		-With the babbling stopped, Bruce flew up with a rope, and we climbed it to follow.
	-Reaching the next surface, we found far more activity than the abandoned area given over to
	 Rovert.
		-There were tiny constructs swarming all over the place, building things from metal.
		-Noticing us, several, then many more, approached us, and lights on their bodies began to
		 blink.
		-Lucien then. . . showed them his sword? Well, actually, he caused it to repeatedly wreath
		 itself in flames and then extinguish. . . blinking back.
		-That actually got somewhere. One of the otherwise silent constructs spoke up, repeating,
		 "Boxes. Safe in boxes."
		-The party fell to arguing with them, there being lots of back and forth along those lines
		 and none of us being to keen to be placed into any kind of box.
		-The construct _did_ mention being "safe from implantation", which called something to mind.
		-"Ohhh," I said. "Can you guys make _small_ boxes? Something we could put on top of our
		  heads?"
		-They proved eager to help and soon we had helmets for those of us that lacked them.
			-I even talked them into making a fashionably red one for me.
		-With the constructs in so good a mood, I figured it was an opportune time to ask them, 
		 "How do we get down to the next layer from here?"
		-The construct said a lot about a "permanent box". Eventually, I worked out it meant a
		 large building a little bit away.
	-We said our goodbyes and approached the building, which was also surrounded by a fair bit of
	 activity: humanoid creatures, marching in uncanny unison.
		-We tried a variety increasingly strident methods for getting their attention, culminating
		 in Maya and Lucien slapping a couple of them, but we got no response from the blank faced
		 people.
		-D'Roc could almost reach the windows of the factory, though, and boosted Lucien up.
		-Lucien reported that, inside, a scorpion was stabbing the heads of golems. . . and also
		 that the window opened.
		-"Well, helmets everyone!" I called out.
		-We clambered through the window, and onto the factory's catwalks, which proved to hang
		 above many levels of conveyor belts, stretching far below the level we'd reached up to the
		 window from.
			-Those conveyors indeed featured many humanoid golems, that some kind of crystalline
			 scorpians were indeed doing. . . something to the heads of.
		-There, we caught sight of someone who was perhaps some kind of supervisor, dressed in
		 coveralls and seemingly patroling the catwalks.
		-Naturally, we hid.
		-Maya attempted some kind of distraction with her illusion cards, calling into being the
		 illusion of a humanoid woman in furs.
		-That seemed to just result in the supervisor turning and jogging off, pulling something
		 from his clothes. Lucien said he could hear the supervisor saying something about needing
		 backup. . .
		-Well, I knew that was likely to mean more, angrier constructs, so I suggested we get the
		 hells out of there.
	-We needed to descend to the next layer, so we opted to use a rope to climb down to one of the
	 conveyer belts we could see, roughly 40' below us.
	-Unfortunately, as the last of us descended, a huge astral construct smashed through the wall
	 near one end of the belt, striding ominously forward.
		-Lucien wasted no time and ran forward to meet it. It swung for him, but he ducked low and
		 then slashed at it repeatedly with his sword to. . . some effect.
		-I being less confident in the impact of arrows on that tower of ectoplasm, I ran at it
		 too. . . and dived between it's legs and through the rent in the wall it came from.
		-I found myself in a shaft, lined with more conveyer belts, that sloped steeply up and down.
		-"I think I found our way down, guys!" I called out.
		-Meanwhile, D'Roc joined Lucien at hacking away at the construct, while Sarge blasted it
		 with flames.
		-For it's part, it struggled to connect with Lucien, though that didn't dissuade it from
		 swinging at him again and again in a flurry of blows.
		-It continued to get the worse of the exchange with the party until it was shattered to
		 slowly dissipating globs of ectoplasm.
	-We followed the shaft downward, emerging into a seemingly endless field of crystalline tubes,
	 many housing various humanoids.
		-There was also an announcement blaring from. . . somewhere, and repeating in various
		 languages instructions to retreat to safety while the emergency is "addressed".
		-Not caring for the sound of that last, we briefly discussed options for a distraction, to
		 cover our escape.
		-I asked Maya if she'd like to play a game of cards and, saying that she'd love to, she
		 drew forth a card and called into being the image of a huge (and distracting) iron golem.
		-She sent it running off down a throughfare, while we hastily headed the opposite direction,
		 losing ourselves in the field of tubes.
	-Soon the sound of pursuit and alarms faded, and we were free to explore the area, to find our
	 way futher into Edric's realm.
	-It was Bruce that identified a tube that differed from the others.
		-Rather than a solid floor, it's base opened into a shaft descending deeper into the plane.
		-However, it was barely big enough for Bruce, and far too small for the rest of us.
		-Sarge saw to fixing that with a spell he named Shatter, crumbling both the tube and the
		 rock of the shaft it sat above, widening the opening.
	-The widened passage led to a layer over which a great cathedral-like structure sprawled,
	 seemingly encompassing the whole plane.
		-On one side of the cloistered courtyard we'd emerged into, there stood a great door, which
		 opened at our arrival, welcoming us inside (though I felt chilled at the sight).
		-Maya, though, drew us up short, and gave a speech. She spoke of our great accomplisments
		 thus far, and the majestic fates that awaited us in the future, and we all took heart.
		-As we walked through the doors, though, we felt a powerful compulsion to kneel.
		-I was intent on dealing from position of strength, though, and, drawing on how Maya's
		 speech left me feeling, I stood tall.
		-We found ourselves before a great adamantine throne, on which was seated Edric.
			-He'd long ago twisted himself far from mortal form, and now was a great, gleaming
			 crystalline figure, strange and alien.
		-My attention, though, was drawn to what stood beside it: a crystal tube with Grimble in it.
		-I didn't hesitate to harangue, yelling, "Hey! That's _my_ righthand gnome!"
		-Edric then spoke, demanding of me, "Did you spread my good word to The Material Plane?"
		 "I thought I was bringing information _back_," I replied.
		 "It flows both ways. . ." the god said. "And what of my ship?"
		 "I. . . replaced it. Why, Jade here is quite the shipwright! Her craftsmanship. . ."
		 "And what of it's crew? Those who set out with you?"
		 "Eh, they didn't last ten minutes. . . But! The crew I've found has done so much. . .
		  It's why I need Grimble back! He's essential to the operation! And, I've brought _your_
		  right hand back to you. . . Jade, where's that rum bottle?"
		 "Ah, Rovert. . . Such a disappointment, what happened. . ."
		-Seeing the god reminisce, Maya spoke up, saying, "Is this really what you wanted, when
		 you were mortal?"
		-That pissed him right off, and he did. . . something. She fell to the ground, facedown.
		-She quickly stirred, though, thankfully, and, seemingly groggy, regained her feet. She then
		 shook her head, as if to clear it, and spoke again, saying, "Lord Edric, what _we_ want
		 is Grimble back. No less and no more. . ."
		 "I bought him," the god replied.
		 "Stole him!" I was quick to correct.
		 "Bought. And let us speak then of what I want. . ." the god began. "Business has slowed.
		  During the last war, anyone would offer up any treasure in exchange for ships and
		  material. I want such markets again."
		 "Well, OK," I replied. "I've got information on that front, angles on offer. Take Maya, for
		  example. She clearly means to be queen of Sasserine, and certainly wouldn't mind an
		  armada. . ."
		-Maya saw no need to deny that, and was, I think, rather intrigued by the notion of a fleet.
		-In any event, she and Edric fell to haggling.
			-He was pushing her for more than simply buying a fleet. He wanted a _war_, something to
			 drive sales to all sides.
			-She, meanwhile, was very insistent that Grimble be returned to us, now and unchanged.
			-For my part, if she was willing to burn her world to give me Grimble back, I guess I
			 wasn't going to stop her. . .
		-It seemed they'd come to terms. A crystal collar formed around Grimble's neck, the tube
		 opened, and then Edric pushed Grimble towards us.
		-"Grimble!" I shouted, stepping towards him. "Long time, no see! . . . are you OK?"
		-But Maya spoke up again before Grimble did. "I said he would be unmolested," she stated,
		 gravely.
		 "He is himself," the god replied. "The collar will simply return him to me, should you not
		  hold to your end of the bargain and sell the fleets."
		-It then became clear that Maya was trying to do _exactly_ what I told her not too, as she
		 inisted, "I said I would _consider_ doing so. And I have. . ."
			-Maya was trying to trick a god. A god of the mind.
			-I think she may have tried going even further, as some of her words seemed freighted
			 with the arcana granted her by her patron wyrm. If so, it would seem to have failed.
			-I cannot say that I can recall for sure what exact words she or the god spoke and
			 agreed to, preoccupied as I was while watching a young girl argue with my worst
			 nightmare over the fate of my friend's soul. . .
			-The two began to argue, but it was clear that Edric was not going to meekly let us
			 claim Grimble through wordplay.
		-As Edric was about to pull Grimble back, Maya drew out the platinum cloak she'd been given
		 by her dragon god and, wrapping it around him, said, "Grimble, at least take your cloak!"
	-In a sudden flash, we were then elsewhere. We stood before a desk, behind which sat a silvery-
	 scaled dragonborn.

9/16/24: The Trial, and the After. . . party
	-This was clearly not where I'd parked my airship. . . a sentiment I gave voice to.
	-"Oh, traffic is down the hall," the dragonborn responded to that.
	-". . . wait. _You're_ the ones here about that gnome," he added.
	 "Oh! Yeah! What do you know about Grimble?" I asked.
	-He went on to explain what we'd asked for by wrapping Grimble in Bahamut's cloak: the judgement
	 of gods.
		-There would be a panel of three gods.
		-"Edric has already chosen a kobold. . . kind-of. . . god?" the scaly functionary said to
		 us. "He's called Kurtulmak. You'll need to pick one judge as well, another lawful god."
			-"Who paid attention that day of class?" I asked. "Maya?"
			-That led to some debate, with Maya listing various lawfully aligned gods.
			-I seized on her mention of Moradin, breaking in and saying, "Oh! Yeah, Moradin would
			  work. Dwarves love gnomes! And gnomes love dwarves. . . and the dwarves we've met like
			  us well, enough. . . Yeah, that'll do!"
		-"There will also be a third, neutral diety on the tribunal, to arbitrate. . ." the
		 dragonborn added.
	-Within seconds, and with another sudden flash, we were in a new room, though one of a common
	 style with the functionary's room.
		-At one table sat Edric, along with a scholarly-looking kobold and several constructs
		 flipping through paperwork.
		-We stood before a table of our own, and there were three empty podiums on a platform before
		 us.
		-In the center of the chamber, there was Grimble, contained within a crystal column.
			-I tentatively waved to him, and received a wave back, but it was slow and. . .
			 multifluous? His arm seemed to blur into many arms, all waving out of sync and at
			 slightly different angles. . .
		-"All rise!" called out a winged, angelic  baliff to our left.
		-The baliff then heralded each god in turn, as they materialized before their podiums. There
		 were:
			-"The Soul Forger, Moradin!"
			-"Death's Guardian, Wee Jas!"
			-"And The Gnomesmasher, Kurtulmak!"
	-Their eyes all turned to us, then, Edric's accusers, as they waited expectantly.
		-"I am no enemy to Edric," I began. "I am a creation of Edric's myself, but one mistreated
		  every step along the way.
		  Grimble, though, was no part of my relationship with Edric, and had his soul claimed just
		  to send me a _message_. 
		  And we would have sought his resurrection! Edric denied life _and_ proper after life to
		  him, over a dispute he was no part of."
		-Edric then droned through his response, saying, "I did not mistreat Fredrick. Everything
		  of his life was as it needed to be, as best served the realms material and divine. Perfect.
		  Grimble died when one of his own companions' own rage was reflected back by a natural
		  formation of crystals. I simply purchased his soul, which no god laid claim do, following
		  the proper procedure."
	-Edric was first to present evidence.
		-He drew forth a string of crystals, in which tiny moving images and, concentrating a moment
		 while holding one, he conjured forth the image of a scene. . . the scene of Grimble's death.
			-I got to witness again his destruction by a burst of terrible energy.
		-Jade called out to the tribunal, though, saying, "This scene has been manipulated, stripped
		 of it's emotional context! It is meant to mislead."
		-Moradin at least was persuaded, and called to see the _whole_ of the context.
			-Mostly, that meant seeing my grieving over poor Grimble. . .
	-Seizing the initiative, Maya then asked to speak on my behalf and, when I gestured that she
	 should go ahead, she proceeded to speech-ify.
		-It was long on tenets of divine law, principals of divine interference, and, perhaps most
		 importantly, flattery of our divine judges.
		-To be honest, it was a bit much to my ears, but also seemed exactly the kind of lengthy
		 polite rambling that our divine judges would want to hear.
		-"Well said!" I shouted out at the end.
	-Following that, Moradin asked to see the crystal containing the scene of Grimble's death, and
	 was duely obliged.
		-The Dwarfather performed some magic, conjuring visions of Grimble's soul going to
		 Glittergold, and then pronounced the crystal a forgery!
			-"The gnome's soul _would_ have been delivered to Garl Glittergold," he said, "But it
			  was snatched away!"
		-"Of course he belonged to Glittergold," I agreed. "He was a paragon of gnomishness, in his
		  illusions and his humor both. Though he seldom thought of the gods, he was Glittergold's
		  through and through."
		-The kobold god was unsurprisingly unpersuaded and yelled out, "It was purchased! Glittergold
		  will not have him!"
	-Wee Jas meanwhile looked stern. . . but skeptical of Kurtulmak, at least.
	-Maya took the opportunity to suggest a remedy, saying, "If I could propose a solution? Grimble's
	  soul could be remanded to _my_ care, and him returned to life? Then, the matter of his soul's
	  destination can be settled by Grimble himself?"
		-That prompted sputtering from Kurtulmak. . . and glaring at Maya from me. _Her_ care?
	-Wee Jas then spoke, saying, "No, not life. . . Something between. Pulled between mortal and god,
	  he will be pulled between life and death, as they fe are."
	-With that the crystal column surrounding Grimble disolved, Grimble spouted butterfly wings, and
	 he began to flutter around the chamber.
	-He only had a few seconds to do so, though, as, in a blink, we found ourselves in a temple of
	 Moradin that. . . wait, this was _Sharaar Kol!_
	-I simply stared at Grimble, hardly having believed he would ever be returned to me. . .
	-That revery was broken by an apology from Maya, who said, "Fred, my request that Grimble be
	  given over to me. . . I only meant to see him returned to life and released.
	 "I. . . I'm sure you meant well," I replied. "I'm just a bit sensitive about gnome-theft right
	  now. . ."
	-"This. . . this deserves a party! The _biggest_ party!" I began to ramble. "We'll get ahold of
	  the party lizard. . . Grimble! We're in Sharaar Kol. . . Lets go to that bar with the dancing!"
	-The two of us began to walk out of the temple and into the corridor, but then I turned around,
	 saying, "Oh, yeah! Jade! I've got a Wand of Sending with a charge left, but can you do anything
	 similar? We should send a message to The Party Lizard!"
		-It turned out she could in fact add some temporary charges to the wand, so we fell to
		 discussing who we should send invites out to.
		-Folks that came to my mind:
			Party Lizard
			"Those deep gnomes we rescued are fun! The ones that think we're gods?"
			"The High Priest of Moradin is cool, and probably right around here somewhere."
			"Who else survived one of my parties. . . Well, you guys. . ."
	-Soon we were at the bar, and all sorts of people were turning up, probably helped by me shouting
	 invites to everyone we passed.
		-As things at the bar began to get rolling, though, Maya was standing off by herself,
		 looking a little shell-shocked, so I walked up to her and thrust a full glass of wine into
		 her hand.
			-"I know that look. . . that's the look of someone who needs to drink something away,"
			 I said to her.
			-"I. . . never met a god before. . ." she began, than chugged the whole glass, proving
			 me right.
		-Soon, some music started up, with a shirtless half-orc on stage yelling, "We are The
		 Bardvarians!" before launching into something loud.
		-A short bit later, several dwarven defenders marched into the bar, shouting, "Make way for
		 his highness!"
			-They were soon followed by the king himself, shouting, "Make way. . . to the bar!
			  We're doing shots!"
			-I insisted the bartender pour a couple into my bottle of Rov-slime, which was met with
			 a suitable thumbs up gesture from the slime.
		-Maya still seemed a bit out of sorts, though, rather than her usual bubbly self.
			-She began to debate aloud what she should do with herself next after. . . all this.
			-She seemed unsure what she wanted now. . . but seized upon Sarge, who had mentioned
			 a long while back wishing to see his homeland again.
				-A chance to focus on another's needs seemed to focus _her_. . . and Sarge certainly
				 _did_ deserve a vacation. Can't say I'd ever been before either, which is a mark in
				 it's favor.
		-After he performed some acrobatics, we also briefly tried to encourage Lucien to become
		 what I billed as "The World's Scariest Devil-Mime".
			-He was not on board. . . though used it to make a horrifying joke, proving the concept
			 had legs.
			-After he started dipping into his Abyssal liqour, he also started mumbling, "Maybe I
			  should go see my family. . . the _good_ ones. . . "
		-Lucien also took a moment to pour some Abyssal Temptation into the Rov-bottle.
			-That resulted in (visible to everyone!) tiny Ed and tiny Fred on it's. . . "shoulders".
			-"Woo! Go slime-Fred!" I called out, as a familiar struggle ensued.
			-My victory was clear, and the slime turned from green to red. . .
		-Grimble, for his part, turned summersaults in the air, until his alcohol content rendered
		 that unwise, and then began to conjure illusory scenes from his weird adventures beyond
		 death.

9/30/24:
	-During the party, I led a very drunk Squee over to Jade, to ask her if if she'd ever heard
	 of "The End of Infinity".
		-(With Squee being unable to die, I saw no reason not to egg him onto terrible feats of
		  liqour consumption.)
		-Jade thought that _did_ sound like something, a term she'd heard to describe the space
		 _between_ planes. A place that still harbored. . . creatures.
		-". . . end? . . . or 'nother gruesome. . . " Squee mumbled.
		 ". . . yeah!" I cut in. "This one of those tentacle monster situations, Jade?"
			-That was just met with a shrug from Jade.
		-"I guess if you were to visit the Negative or Positive energy planes. . ." Jade began.
		 "Trrrriiied," Squee slurred in response.
		-That met with some incredulity from my . . . friends, and D'Roc to ask, "How long have you
		  been around, Squee?"
			-By way of response, he pulled out a small, tattered book, and began leafing drunkenly
			 through it.
			-It was filled with crude tallies, which he dragged his finger along haphazardly while
			 muttering various numbers before blurting, "Lost count. *Hic*"
			-After some further questions from various people, they eventually concluded it had been
			 _at least_ a millenia.
				-That's a hell of a long time. I wonder if he can trade his "curse" to me. . .
	-The dwarvern bar actually managed to _run out of beer_, to much jeering from all around.
		-"Well get some more!" I demanded of the bartender.
		 "You don't understand!" he shouted back. "The whole damned _city_ is out now!"
		 "I thought you dwarves were supposed to be industrious! Running out of beer. . . Who can
		  conjure us some more!" I walked off shouting.
		-Jade saved the day by conjuring up more kegs.
	-Eventually, the party did wind down. I woke the next morning, still in the bar and thoroughly
	 hung over, surrounded by scattered deep gnomes.
		-It was the breakfast rush that woke me, an assortment of dwarves digging into food and ale
		 before shifts in the mines.
	-Rather than endure any more of their noise or their joking(?) offers to pick up a mining shift,
	 we gathered ourselves up and got to leaving.
		-On the way out of the bar, D'Roc pointed out the glint of. . . glass? In a nearby alley?
		-Bruce saw it too, and I was quick to ask, "The glint of gems maybe? Treasure?!?"
		 "No. . ." D'Roc said. "It moved?"
		 "Moved?!? Some construct or the like? Which way was it?!? I'm going the other!" I rambled.
		-I began to hurry off in a random direction, but then a voice called out saying, "Wait!
		  Stay in the frame!"
		-A trio of odd looking humanoids then emerged from the alley, one of them bearing a crystal
		 studded device.
		-That last still had me quite alarmed, but they eventually got it across that they wanted an
		 interview, for some kind of interplanar newspaper.
		-Hearing that, I said, "Ah! Adoring fans! I get those _all_ the time, and hardly _ever_ get
		 them killed!"
		-They looked a bit alarmed at the last bit, but pressed on, asking for the story of my
		 recent court case.
		-I began to regale them with the tragic story of my childhood in Edric's realm.
		-After several minutes of that, one broke in with a question, saying, "Do you have any
		  family? Someone who could corroborate your story?"
		 "Sure! I replied, pulling out a half full bottle. "This is my great, great, great, great,
		  great, Uncle Rov!"
		-That bottle proved to contain rum, though, so, after a swig, I spent another moment digging
		 the bottle of slime out of my haversack.
		-"Uncle Rov! My adoring fans want to interview us!" I said, addressing the bottle.
		-By way of response, the slime formed a head and the approximation of some hair, and then
		 smoothed the "hair" back with a psuedopod.
		-"Why are you in a bottle?" one of the reporters then asked. "Seems like a story there?"
		 "Well, your conciousness gets fractured, manifests as slime, gets scooped up by your
		  nephew. You know how it goes!"
		 ". . . sure. Bit played out, though, don't you think? What of your time with Edric? Any
		  lovers? What about adventures?"
		 "Lovers. . . aren't really Edric's thing. But, adventures? Sure! Why, early after his
		  ascension, he and his Brotherhood fought another god, destroying him with a Sphere of
		  Annihilation!"
		-They spent some time writing that down, then turned back to me, asking if I had any
		 adventures of my own to report.
		-"Tons! We've fought dinosaurs, undead dinosaurs, octopuses, octopus demons. . . all sorts
		  of stuff!" I replied. "How much time do you have?"
		-One of them consulted a _very_ elaborate watch, muttering something about time getting
 		 awfully complicated when you travel the planes, before calling out, "6 points."
		 "Perfect!" I replied, without missing a beat. "Then you have time for my greatest triumph,
		  at least: the recent court case!"
		-I then went into how I was terribly wronged, how Maya's friendship with Bahamut enabled our
		 appeal to the court, and how my many cunning strategems won the day.
		-Eventually, the one with the watch cut me off saying, "I think that's enough for now"
		-"Here's my card," another said, handing it to me, and than all three of them disappeared
		 in a flash of light.
		-"Let me see that card," Jade said, taking it form my hands.
			-After examining it a moment, she pronounced it a plane shift scroll, targeted to a
			 specific plane, a place she said was a kind of news room?
			 "Ah! So I'm set up for whenever I want to retire to a career of punditry, then?
			  Excellent!" I said.
		     Then, after a pause, I added, "Lots of aging pirates retire to be come news anchors.
		      Happens all the time."
	-After that, we returned to our ongoing discussion of what to do next, a thing I was rather
	 sanguine about, having just gotten the thing that I wanted.
		-We talked again about Squee's problem, inspiring me to ask, "Oh! That Sphere of Annihilation
		  The Brotherhood used. . . I wonder if that is still around, and would work?"
		-Ultimately, though, we settled on the treasure map. It sounded lot less dangerous than
		 Annihilation and such. . .  and, because, _treasure map_.
	-The one landmark on the map was the city of Graywall, a few days flight Northeast of Sharaar Kol.
	-So, we set about taking on supplies and rounding up our hung over crew members. Soon, we were
	 aloft again.
		-We opted to take more or less the shortest route. . . across the turbulent and dangerous
		 skies over the Graywall mountains.
		-That was because it was over those very same mountains, on the trip to The Shining Valley
		 and it's gnomish village, we had spied that floating platform, and Jade was still quite
		 keen on investigating it.
	-The journey was wracked by stormy weather.
		-At one point, a gnomish crewman almost went overboard, but I lassoed him with a handy line,
		 and hauled him back across the deck with help from D'Roc
	-We had a decent sense of where the platform was and, as we neared where we saw it, D'Roc
	 claimed he could _smell_ it, or at least the way it disturbed the air currents we were sailing
	 through.
		-Well, his nose didn't lead us astray, and instead _did_ lead us to the platform, sitting in
		 a volume of air the rain mysteriously did not touch.
		-On top of that, the platform was also weirder than it was before, with a series of flickering
		 images playing out across it's surface.
		-Sarge suspected an illusion, a conclusion Jade and Grimble nodded sagely in agreement with.
		-He said such things had been common in his war, as a way of concealing ships and other
		 large objects, to disguise them as wild magic.
		-We discussed poking at it in various ways: throwing something at it or shooting it with a
		 cannon, but ultimately settled on a conjured gust of wind from Sarge, as our gentlest option.
		-That may not have been our _best_ option, though, as, once Sarge finished the innvocation,
		 we all began to float, and scrambled to grab ahold of some bit of the ship.
		-Jade shouted something about it functioning as a magic inverter, rebounding magical energies
		 back at us, and we all had to wait a moment for the effect to end.
		-D'Roc then _did_ throw a rock at the. . . thing, confirming, yep, it's an illusion, but
		 Jade also claimed that it was _reacting_ to us, intelligently, and perhaps was being
		 actively controlled.
		-There was no thump or anything like that, though, that anyone heard from the rock.
		-"Well," I asked, "Who wants to go see what's inside there? Folks with wings?"
		-I got a healthy number of volunteers (well, unhealthy, given the danger involved), and
		 Bruce and Sarge were soon getting ready to fly into the illusion. Jade broke in and
		 suggested that she could make D'Roc fly with a minute's prep, and soon she was riding a
		 flying minotaur off with them as I saluted (a thing I'm not sure I _can_ do not
		 sarcastically).
	-After they were gone for roughly an hour, the illusion began to slowly move towards our ship.
		-When the lookout in the pointed that out, I sprang into action, calling out to the crew,
		 "Full speed in reverse! It's coming at us!"
		-A few minutes later though, Bruce, in the bigger-bat-thing form he often shifted into,
		 came flapping out of the illusion towards us.
		-I called out to him as he neared, saying, "What's going on? What's in there?"
		 "A ship! And it's mad captain!" Bruce shouted in reply. "He stopped time and took us
		  captive! You need to negotiate for the others' release! Slow down!"
		 "Huh. . . Sarge was right, it was hiding a ship. . . Well, trim the sails! Bring us into
		  the illusion at docking speed!" I called out to the crew.
	-As our ship passed within the illusion, I could suddenly see a gigantic ship before us.
		-It was painted with a name, The Storm's Ascent.
		-We pulled alongside it and the crew got a gangplank into position.
		-What greeted us was a warforged with eight arms, bedecked in a splendid, if tattered,
		 miltary uniform. Behind him, the away party sat in chains, all save Jade who had been
		 apparently allowed her freedom.
		-The captain greeted me and said, "Call me Red," a name his cloak indeed matched.
		 "Oh ho! Good taste!" I replied. "I'm _Fred_ the Red! Well met!"
		 Opening with an accusation, my opposite number said, "So you're the pirate."
		 "Well, don't think I've ever captured a ship. . . not that I'd turn another one down mind
		  you. But I'm forever getting called all sorts of names. . ."
		 "They called _me_ a traitor," the warforged mumbled darkly. "Couldn't in good conscious do
		  what they asked me too. . ."
		 "I know a thing or two about that!" I commiserated. "The god that sent me out on a scouting
		  mission with my first ship, he's a dick! Why he kidnapped my gnome and dared to. . . But,
		  trauma stories are best told over drinks!
		 "Grimble!" I called to my fairly fey friend. "I still haven't seen Lucien for a bit. . .
		  but do you think he's got a bottle of that Abyssal Temptation below decks? See if you can
		  find one!"
		 Turning back to the captain, I said, "You'll love the stuff! It's imported!"
		-The captain then went back to babbling about the assassins that doubtlessly had been sent
		 after him and other such ancient history while Grimble went off in search of a bottle.
		-A short while later, Grimble returned with one of the distinctive bottles and handed it to
		 the captain.
		-He uncorked it and then paused. Perhaps thinking of those assasins, he turned to Sarge and
		 said, "You first."
		-Sarge nodded and, taking the bottle in one manacled hand, took a swig and, with a look of
		 concentration on his face, managed to show no outward signs of the liquors more unusual
		 effects.
		-Satisfied, the captain took his own drink, and soon was yelling at tiny figures on his
		 shoulders. . . a thing actually rather in keeping with the rest of his behavior thus far.
		-I took the opportunity to quickly draw my rapier and stab the captain in the gap between
		 two of the plates that made up his outer carapace.
		-D'Roc and Sarge were quick to join my attack, with Sarge blasting the madman with a magic
		 shout while D'Roc wrapped his chains around the captain's neck and tried to strangle him.
		-Soon, the captain dropped lifeless to the deck. . . but, as he did, a steady beeping began
		 to come from somewhere within the ship.
		-Jade looked alarmed. Well, we all did, but her especially, and she ran off in the direction
		 of the ship's helm.
		-I began to edge my way over to the gangplank and when, after a minute or so, the beeping
		 stopped and the ship began to instead list sharply to one side, I ran across, back to my
		 ship.
		-I was joined in that by most of the party, save D'Roc who went running after Jade.
		-I grabbed a line, tossing one end after them, and then began tying the other to my ship's
		 rail.
		-Soon, D'Roc was running back, Jade slung over one shoulder, and grabbed for the line as
		 the deck tilted faster and faster under him.
		-The crew hauled them back aboard as the other ship fell from beneath them, to a spectacular
		 crash in the mountains below.
		-We all looked over the rail at the wreckage below, most seemingly as wistful as I at the
		 loss of that beautiful warship.
		-Jade immediately began to talk of salvaging the thing, and Sarge had apparently been wise
		 enough to do some salvaging on the way out, presenting her with a wand he'd taken from the
		 fallen mad-captain.
		-After some extensive study, and consulting with Sarge, Jade pronounced it the warship's
		 control rod, and also a Wand of Command in it's own right.
		-She remained very much intent on salvaging what we could form the ship, despite the
		 mountainous terrain it's wreckage was spread across, and I was all for it, thinking of
		 how it's artifice could be repurposed for our own ship.


10/28/24:
	-Intent on that salvage, we brought the ship down lower, over the crashsite.
		-The winds grew stronger and more turbulent nearer the mountains, so I was busy barking
		 orders as the crew rushed all over the place, trying to keep the ship under control.
		-The wreckage was. . . flickering. Strangely.
			-Jade deemed it some kind of arcane energy, suggesting it was perhaps coming from the
			 warship's engines.
		-There was no surface suitable for actually _landing_ our ship, so, once we neared the
		 crashsite, we lowered ropes and climbed down.
	-Once on the mountainside, we sought a way up the sharp slope.
		-We pooled our ropes and climbing gear, giving charge of them to Sarge, who apparently
		 wore dragon-themed boots with a climbing effect.
		-He scurried up the snowy slope, and _attempted_ to anchor the ropes to the mountainside,
		 for the rest of us to climb up, but they came undone with the slightest tug.
			-Can't _believe_ he used to serve aboard ships. . .
		-Jade solved the issue, though, by granting a similar spell effect to D'Roc, who then
		 _carried_ most of us up the steep slope, his feet (Hooves? What's inside those boots?)
		 glued to the mountain by magic.
		-Part way up, though, Lucien called out from where he hung from D'Roc's back, saying, "Look!
		  There's something moving in the snow!"
		-We followed his pointing, seeing large, shadowy figures approaching through the snow
		 flurries.
		-Any illusion that they came in peace was quickly shattered by the howling of wolves.
		-Moments later, as they approached through the snow, the figures revealed themselves to be
		 a band of various giants, preceded by several large, white wolves. . . 
		-. . . and Lucien, with haste-enhanced speed, rushed towards them himself, cutting down the
		 leading wolf.
		-With that, the battle was joined, with us hurling spells down the slope while the giants
		 hurled rocks upward.
		-For our part, Grimble conjured an illusory white dragon, bursting from "beneath" the snow,
		 roaring and snapping, while I stared down the biggest frost giant, their apparent leader,
		 and locked his brain.
			-The wolves, and a couple of the giants, ran in fear of the gargantuan dragon while
			 their leader stared blankly ahead.
			-With that accomplished, the two of us wisely sought some cover to hide behind.
		-Sarge's conjured bursts of flames proved devestatingly effective, but one of the frost
		 giants managed to tackle Lucien, and he fell in the snow, wrestling with his enormous
		 opponent.
		-D'Roc, nearly the size of the giant, came to Lucien's rescue, running at them and slamming
		 into the giant, pushing the giant off Lucien and goring the huge humanoid with his horns.
		-One of the giants hit Maya with a thrown boulder, staggering her and nearly knocking her
		 off her feet.
			-In response she turned to the giant and stared him down. I think she may have been
			 casting some spell but, if so, I did not see what it did. The giant, in any event
			 seemed unphased.
		-Eventually, the series of spells hurled at his vicinity incinerated the stupified leader
		 of the giants (along with any pretense Grimble's dragon was real), freeing Grimble and I
		 to focus on other things.
			-I used that opportunity to take careful aim at the nearest giant and, popping up from
			 my cover, lodged an arrow between his ribs, before ducking back down.
			-Grimble made to follow my example, holding his crossbow and beginning to stand up, but
			 I yanked him back down, saying, "Hey. You already basically died once. Don't be so
			  eager for a repeat performance."
		-The fight wore on and, though mostly one sided, even formidble D'Roc fell for a bit beneath
		 a giant's fierce blows, but he was soon back on his feet, some of his wounds healed by a
		 potion flown over by Maya's familiar.
		-Eventually, the remaining couple of giants turned to flee, though that didn't stop me from
		 loosing more arrows after them.
			-I'm not above shooting a man in the back.
	-After the fight, we searched through the bodies of the giants.
		-More salvage. . .
		-Sadly, the weapons of the frost giants turned out to be made of ice, pretty much ruling
		 out any resale value.
		-Their leader had a sweet magic belt, though, and they had a fair amount of coin between
		 them.
	-Returning to the climb, we reached the wreckage of the warship a short while later.
		-Peering through a rent in the ship's mangled hull, we could see the ship's engines. . .
		 which were surrounded by a continuous lightshow of arcing energies.
		-At our urging, Jade stepped forward to examine the matter more closely, but jumped back as
		 an arc of energy caught her foot.
			-The wound, rather than the burn we expected, was more of a. . . blackening, necrotic
			 affair, suggesting the energy was not simply lightning.
		-Maya, ever the historian, was excited that the aft of the ship was most intact.
			-She mentioned she hoped there might be log books and the like, discussing the ship's
			 service and travels.
			-Well, I _was_ rather fond of the color of the captain's wardrobe. . .
			-Maya then clarified her intentions, suggesting that the log books may disclose the
			 location of old _armories_, from the war, thing perhaps stocked with ship parts and
			 the like.
			-_That_ had me rubbing my hands. . .
		-"Oh!" I then blurted out. "Maya's mention of the captain reminds me of something! Didn't
		  Sarge grab some kind of control device for the ship? That wand-like thing? Maybe it can
		  be used to control the engines?
		-My suggestion unsurprisingly proved brilliant and, drawing out the wand, Jade fiddled with
		 if for a bit and was eventually able to stop the arcing energies.

11/11/24:
	-"Is that thing safe to approach now, Jade?" I asked.
	 "Uh. . . I think so?"
	 "Great! We've got a rescue to do! The air elementals that powered this ship, they've been
	  trapped, what, decades?"
		-I then called out in Auran, "Hello?"
		-But, if I got any reply, well, we were on a windswept mountainside and the language sounds
		 like wind in the first place.
	-It seemed like we needed to get closer, so Jade and Maya discussed some options and settled on
	 what turned out to be a _quite_ impressive Lute (of Building) solo, substantially repairing the
	 damaged, and previously shakey, wreckage.
	-In response, though, flashing arcs of lightning again began to dance over the ship's hull and
	 engines.
		-In fact, the patterns. . . seemed less than random.
		-Our arcanists fell to discussing the matter.
			-They concluded that these _were_ the elementals that had been powering the ship, but
			 that they were also somehow supercharged.
			-They discussed a plane of origin that had greater levels of elemental energy, as well
			 some arcane transformation process, one related to dragons, and perhaps the process
			 that _made_ Sarge something dragon-like.
			-In any event, the lute's magic seemed to have pacified them somewhat.
		-"So, these are the elementals then?" I asked and, seeing more nods than shrugs, I called
		 again to the dancing arcs in Auran, saying, "Hey there!"
		-The lightening arcs continued their dance, but it _changed_. It was a response.
		-Maya's a dancer to rival even I, and is perhaps somewhat bolder than me (probably due to
		 her gentler upbringing), so she was quick to follow their lead and engage in a kind of
		 _interpretive_ dance, questioning them, after a fashion, about their nature.
		-They responded with images of dragons imbuing something (them?) with lightning energy,
		 only for that all to be stuffed into some kind of device.
			-We also got a scene of warforged marching off to, well, war.
			-Maya recognized the banner in that scene, that of House Deneith, one of the ruling
			 houses of Khorvaire, people known to consort with The Cult of the Dragon Below.
				-Their banner bore a lion, a dragon, and a minotaur.
		-"These Deneith pricks are the ones who bound you to this engine, huh?" I asked the
		 arcing elementals.
			-By way of response, the arcs formed a giant face, which then nodded.
		-"Jerk move," I sympathized. "But, how did you like the sailing life?"
			-This time, we got a whole saga.
			-Their arcs formed a globe, featuring a supercontinent one that, as we watched, was
			 shattered by a great hammer, with the pieces drifting into the shapes of continents
			 we know today.
			-Then, we got to watch a series of battles, nations rising and falling, and great
			 catastophes, all playing out in miniature across the globes surface.
				-I actually learned quite a lot. This electric play was a lot more exciting than
				 history class (everyone got a +5 to Knowledge(History)).
			-With that, they managed to also convey that they had been around for a _long_ time,
			 involved with airships for much of it.
		-"OK, so, _dedicated_ sailors, huh? Me too! You know, we're always looking for experienced
		  crew. . . Our elementals serve freely too. None of this bound to the engines shit. . .
		  You'll love Patches and Peggy! Just watch out when Peggy starts swinging that wooden leg
		  around. At least I _think_ it's a leg. . ."
			-That triggered another show, the globe shrinking, or us receding from it, and then up,
			 past other globes, until all that was contained in one great crystal sphere which was,
			 in turn, soon one tiny crystal sphere among many, pouring through a great hour glass.
			-The more studious among us mumbled about a multi-verse, planes upon planes separated
			 into different spheres.
			-The elementals clearly yearned for other spheres, conveying a desire to leave this one
			 that they'd resided for so long within.
			-Jade even thought that travel between such things was one of the capabilities of this
			 ships wonderous engine, though the damage to it prevented that until substantial
			 repairs were done.
				-"Well, the ability to run _even farther_ away from some folks in my life would be
				  pretty welcome. . ." I responded.
	-Well, with all this interest in a "spelljammer drive", we fell to discussing how we could
	 continue our efforts to salvage the ship.
		-The engine was _immense_. It alone would never fit in our hold.
			-It's 125' x 25' x 15'.
		-So, we started talking about whether we could build some kind of frame we could lift with
		 our ship, perhaps from the warship's remains.
		-Or perhaps we should fortify _this_ area, and create some shelter from the elements, to
		 undertake some serious work on site?
	-With the salvage details still under debate, we figured we should also search through the
	 rest of the before making an final decisions.
		-We turned up some coins and some expensive-looking artworks.
		-It was the captain's quarters that proved especially interesting.
			-There, Maya's eyes alighted upon an especially fine pair of boots, but, when she
			 reached out to touch them, they teleported across the room. . . and began to talk.
			-In the tones of an old sailor, the boots inquired after their captain, and we had to
			 break the news about the long isolation and undeniable madness of the warforged skipper
			 that I stabbed, and his scuttling of the warship.
				-(I glossed over the stabbing bit.)
				-It took some doing, but the boots were eventually persuaded of the captain's
				 madness, especially after they got a sense of how long it had been.
					-They seemed especially hurt that the captain hadn't called on his "first mate"
					 in that time.
				-I saw no reason to mention the stabbing bit.
				-They introduced themselves as Jaspar.
					-"Ah! On account of the brown leather, eh?" I responded. "I like a good
					  wardrobe-and-name theme. . ."
				-When the boots proposed a drinking contest to determine who was the captain now,
				 I knew they were my kind of people. . . er, footwear.
				-I eagerly accepted, and the boots designated D'Roc the referee.
				-"3, 2, GO!" I called out, hoisting the rum bottle I was given to my lips.
				-The boots laces pulled their own bottle over, tipping it into one of the shoes.
				-D'Roc soon called the boots out, for the splashing of liquid he could hear on the
				 other side of the cabin door.
					-"What? It's no different than it going down his stomach. . ." the boots groused
					 as I seized the distraction to keep drinking and try to pull ahead.
					-That shit stopped soon enough anyways, the boots perhaps out of charges, and
					 the voice emanating from the boot without a bottle stuck in it began to slur.
				-I had to lean on my mental powers to push myself to keep rushing towards alcohol
				 poisoning, but also noticed my bottle was not emptying it as it should, it being
				 seemingly endless, and perhaps another trick.
				-I'm fuzzy on what happened from there, but clearly I won by disqualification,
				 having at least cheated far less _visibly_ (if my inborn powers are even cheating).
	-The rest of what I remember from the night was trying to sleep beneath a moth-eaten blanket
	 (which smelled of vomit for some reason) while the sounds of music and construction _both_ JUST
	 WOULD NOT KNOCK IT OFF!
