12/16/24:
	-When I could no longer manage more of anything resembling sleep, I got up, wiped off some mess,
	 and stumbled forth, pulling on my new friend Jaspar as I did so.
		-I did _ask_ first:
			"So, Jaspar. . . that rum last night, that felt like the origin of a friendship to me,
			 right? In light of that, mind if I, uh. . . put my feet inside you?"
			". . . I've never been asked quite like that before. . . Well, what's the hygiene
			 situation? Do you powder?"
			"Hmm. . . the inside of you sure smells like rum at the moment. . . and so do I. Guess
			 we can't make it worse?"
	-My crew had been busy in my absence (of consciousness), and I found the wreckage surrounded by
	 a formidable stone wall, the wall itself camouflaged with snow piled against it.
	-I didn't have much time to admire the work, though, as Lucien reported seeing, down the
	 mountain, the glint of what he thought might be a spyglass.
		-Peering down the mountain some more, Lucien thought he might have seen something he termed
		 a "githyanki", some kind of humanoid from the Astral Plane.
			-Well, maybe not originally, Jade clarified. She infact had heard rumors of them being
			 sited around crash sites and natural disasters lately too. . .
		-We talked about talking it out, but, if they're interested in crash sites, well, this one
		 is ours and I sure as the hells ain't giving it up.
		-So, that left intimidation and worse.
		-With them not attacking quite _yet_, we had options to prepare.
			-Maya through out enlisiting gravity to our cause, causing an avalanche or the like.
			-I also asked Jade, "Jade, is any of the ship's artillery still in shape? Or easily
			  repaired? That'd offer the possibility of an avalanche _or_ more direct action. . ."
				-She and Sarge fell to discussing the matter, and seemed confident they could get
				 something working.
		-While we prepped, Lucien pointed out something else alarming: the sun seemed to be getting
		 _dramatically_ brighter, to a degree that, now that he pointed it out, must clearly be
		 unnatural.
			-There goes our snow cover, then, and maybe more badness besides.
		-We debated more prep, but then Lucien blurted out, ". . . someone just tried to banish me."
			-"Jade," I asked, "What's the range on that? Are they already here?"
			 ". . . It's close," she confirmed.
			 "Shit. They're here!"
		-We began to cast our eyes about, Lucien spotted a humanoid creeping up, brandishing a holy
		 symbol.
		-Lucien _also_ put together the sun, the holy symbol, and, now that he mentioned it, the
		 feint whiff of garlic and ran after the humanoid (who turned and fled) yelling, "I'm not a
		 vampire, damn it!"
			-Lucien easily caught up, and started a discussion I was a bit far to hear.
		-After a short conversation, the humanoid disappeared, and Lucien returned.
			-He summarized the conversation saying, yeah, it thought he was a vampire, and was
			 worried about the "planar technology" of the wreckage falling into the hands of. . .
			 someone, and their airship armada.
		-Well, while I was still in favor of our artillery as the solution, but there _was_ more we
		 could learn here.
			-I checked with Jaspar, and, indeed, as he had demonstrated when cheating during our
			 rum drinking contest, he could teleport stuff, and said his limit would be three of us.
			-So, we put together an away party of Lucien, Grimble, and myself.
			-We made no effort to conceal ourselves, since this was a parlay, but _did_ do the most
			 intimidating walk we could manage, which was quite scary, between Lucien and I.
			-As we neared the camp, we hailed them, and a representative came out to talk.
				-"You walk like warriors, not just treasure hunters as we'd expected," the gleaming-
				 armored and green-skinned humanoid said to us by way of greeting. "We did not wish
				  the ship's technology to fall into the wrong hands."
				 "It _is_ quite the treasure," I replied, "But not something we're going to treat
				  lightly. . . or give up lightly. You seem worried about some third party, though.
				  I'd like to learn more about that. . ."
				 "Do any of you have magic in your blood?" the creature then asked.
				-We had looked one to another, the wizard, the planar half-breed, and the whatever
				 I am, and then asked a bunch of clarifying questions.
					-Ultimately, it seemed like his main concern was _sorcerors_. At least Lucien
					 _kind of_ counted, but was less _refined_ than what he said his foe sought.
					-We pointedly _did not_ mention Sarge. . . but should warn him.
				-The githyanki then recommended that, if we employed the ship we were salvaging, we
				 would need protection, and offered that of the Githyanki Empire, but would be said
				 that we would then besubject to the Lich Queen's orders.
				-Changing the subject, I then asked, "Well, can you put a name to this blood
				  drinking nightmare you're concerned about?"
					-"I'm not sure it can be translated. . ." he warned and, indeed the Astral
					 gibberish he then uttered was unintelligible to the three of us.
					-He did, though, speak of entire planes stripped of their blood, saying they
					 seem to be collecting it. . .
				-"Well. . . we're normally freebooters," I began, returning to his offer, "But, if
				  we do seek protection, how do we get in contact?"
					-"Who is your communications officer?" he asked, and we eventually clarified
					 that we would need someone to cast Sending.
					-I said that was well within our abilities and asked his name, which he gave as
					 "R'san".
				-We then took our leave and returned to the ship (on foot, since it wasn't an
				 emergency, tempted though I was to do otherwise, given the slope).
	-By the time we got back to the ship, Maya's Lyre strumming had essentially all the non-magical
	 portions of the warship repaired.

1/6/25:
	-Despite the new revelations about the hazards of traveling between multiverses / crystal
	 spheres / whatever, we were still intent on it after some discussion.
		-Jade _did_ warn us, though, that we had no navigation system for this.
	-So, our course decided, we set about salvaging that engine.
		-D'Roc began hacking away at the structure of the ship, to free the engine.
		-Meanwhile, Maya, with her lyre, played and built a frame to lift the engine with our own
		 shift.
		-Despite my expert guidance, our ship strained to lift the salvaged equipment from the
		 warship's wreckage.
		-Sarge volunteered overcharging the elementals of our own ship's engine again, but,
		 remembering the damage that did to our last ship, I suggested instead the help of our new
		 dragon-lightning elemental friends, invested as they are in the project of getting this
		 engine back together.
		-Consulting Jade, yeah, she thought they might be able to provide some additional oomph for
		 our engine, so they joined our existing air elementals in their labor.
	-But, of course, something went wrong. . .
		-Those lightning elementals added their effort by manipulating the _salvaged_ engine, now
		 at least tied to our existing ship. . . 
		-. . . and, in a flash, we, our ship, and all found ourselves in a vast, gray expanse.
		-That caused some alarm, but thankfully Jade recognized it as The Astral Plane.
		-"Well," I said, "I guess that's more or less what these new engines are supposed to do. . .
		  So, I guess this is kind of a step in the right direction. Jade! What do you need to
		  fully repair these things?"
		-"Time," she replied, but also apparently some supplies, so despite that crystal's mostly
		 endless supply of time, we needed to find something that wasn't gray nothingness.
			-"Well, can you at least get us back to The Material Plane?" I asked her.
			 "I can get _us_ back. . . but not the ship," she replied.
			 "Ah. It _is_ rather dear to me," I said. "The engines are _supposed_ to do that for
			  us. What do you need to get that working, Jade?"
			 "This is the plane of transit. . . Maybe something native to The Astral can help?"
		-So, we set about searching for. . . well, anything, in this vast expanse.
			-Jade offered the intriguing observation that Bag of Holding are actually backed by
			 small, folded pockets of The Astral Plane.
				-". . . does that mean we can _pick_ those pockets?" I asked.
				 "Well. . . maybe?" she replied. "First you'd have to _find_ them and, well, The
				  Astral is _infinite_."
			-Maya volunteered that dragons can (probably) smell gold, and consulted her familiar.
				-Sniffing about, Paziameira the tiny dragon said, "Huh. . . I do detect a faint
				  whiff of silver?"
		-That was good enough for me, so Paziameira pointed us in the direction and away the ship
		 sailed.
	-After we traveled. . . some(?) distance, we could see a gray, smokey fog, on the horizon.
		-As we got nearer, several of us took a look at it through the spyglass, and Maya noted
		 that it appeared to have a humanoid shape, and wore two silver bracelets that were
		 presumably what Paziameira had smelled.
		-"Well, I know Auran and, smoke-man, so I figure Auran or Ignan are both good bets," I
		 volunteered.
		-So I hailed the. . . whatever, calling out, "Ho there! We're a bit lost. . . Mind if we
		  ask for directions?"
		-In response, the smoke-thing disappeared, and suddenly appeared aboard our ship, towering
		 over even D'Roc.
		-I quickly stepped forward to great the. . . whatever, saying, "Hi! Fred the Red here! It's
		  a pleasure to meet you! We wanted to. . . Wait where are my manners?!? Would you like
		  something to drink?"
		-"Well, of course!" the fog bank answered, and conjured a pair of whiskey glasses
		 "Nice trick!" I complemented the cloud. "I've got a trick of my own: endless rum! Good
		  thing too, as you're a big one! Tell me when!"
		-The necessary addressed and drinks in hand, the foggy figure introduced himself as "The
		 Great Wizard Martek" and, as we got to small talk, he asked, "What year is it?"
		 "That depends on where you're from," Maya chimed in.
		 "That it does!" the being replied. "Where are you from?"
		 "We're recently arrived from The Material!" I supplied. "We were messing about with a
		  magical artifact, one thing led to another, and suddenly we're on The Astral Plane. You
		  know how it is, seeing as you're a wizard and all. . .
		 "Indeed I do!" Martek agreed. "Well, it's been some time since last I was there. . . Tell
		  me, do the giants still rule the place?"
		-Not as far as we were aware, so we informed him as much, to his apparent delight, as
		 apparently it was the giants that exiled him to The Astral, long ago.
		-He then asked if we wouldn't happen to have a giant skull by any chance.
			-Maya offered a giant dragon skull (apparently we kept one), proposing exchanging it
			 for his bracelets.
			-Though he commented that such things have power, he wasn't much interested.
			-As he explained, he needed the skull of a giant descended from those that banished him
			 to be able to return to The Material Plane.
			-Nonetheless, Maya tried to sell him on the skull anyways, offering to throw in the
			 celebrated Flumph's Blue Salt ("Great wizard already, it'll make you a great _chef_
			 too!" I added) and, when that was not enough, some soup.
				-"Can I try the soup?" the wizard asked, leading to some cooking on Maya's part,
				 with flumph-provided mushrooms, flame from Paziameira, vegetable slicing from
				 Lucien, and, of course the blue salt.
				-Tasting it, Martek pronounced it good. . . but still wasn't going to be parting
				 with those bracelets.
			-Well, if it's a particular flavor of giant skull he's dead set on, we could certainly
			 keep our eyes out once we found our way back to The Material.
				-Maya thought to inquire, "If we _can_ obtain one, how would we find you?"
				-By way of answer, he gave us a _different_ bracelet, from which dangled four
				 charms. He touched one, which turned a smokey gray, and said that it could be used
				 to call him to us from any point on The Astral Plane.
		-Maya then suggested pancakes, to follow the soup, which we all enthusiastically agreed to.
			-That enthusiasm was somewhat dampered when she suggested that they'd be mushroom
			 pancakes, but we didn't let that entirely deter us.
			-"Grimble!" I called out. "You're an alchemist! Think you could make a syrup from rum?"
				-He did indeed, to much delight.
		-Through out most of this, with only the occasional pancake break, Jade worked on the
		 engines, using that time crystal.
			-Ducking down to where she was doing so, we saw. . . multi-Jade: a flurry of Jades
			 rushing about and working on various portions of the project.
			-Maya tried to touch one, but it was like trying to grasp one of Grimble's illusions,
			 despite the physical progress she was making.
		-Well, leaving Jade to that, we returned to the deck, where Martek was still (somewhat
		 confusingly, given his semi-substantial form) eating pancakes.
		-Eventually, we discussed seeking the aid of the Githyanki, there being a standing offer
		 there, they being (sort of) native to the plane, and they being familiar with the engine
		 technology.
		-Martek knew the way to their Lich Queen and, with some arcane gestures, conjured some form
		 of navigation system for us, with only one set of coordinates within.
	-Saying our goodbyes to Martek, we sailed there and found a floating city of many towers.
		-As we neared the the ring of airships circling structure, I was subjected to a horrid voice
		 ringing in my mind, barking, "Surrender and prepare to be boarded!"
			-"Well, they're hailing us, folks," I relayed to my crew. "Stand down and prepare to
			  greet the welcomong party.
		-One of their ship pulled alongside us and a githyanki sailor called over, "If you come to
		  do hommage to our queen, those pathetic iron tubes you call weaponry disgrace you!"
		 "I have weapons," Maya replied, pointing to D'Roc and Sarge.
		-Lucien looked terribly insulted to not be included and, puffing up his chest, yelled, "Send
		  your fiercest warrior over and I'll show you what I can do! Face me in a duel!"
	-The githyanki took up Lucien's challenge, and sent over their champion.
		-What ensued alternated between a blur of swords and shouted insults.
		-Lucien drew first blood, though, and made the impression we were looking for.
		-Their champion _did_ go out of his way to insult my ship, though. . .
	-We were directed to a dock low on the structure and, as we disembarked, we found ourselves at
	 the base of a _looong_ staircase.
		-Another insult. . .
		-The short trip to the dock, we were also shadowed by a colossal red dragon.
			-So, hooray, a show of power too. I like these jackasses about as well as I do Edric.
	-Well, after an interminable climb, we were led to the Lich Queen's throne room.
		-Her intimidating decore and wardrobe made quite the impression. Enough of an impression,
		 in fact that D'Roc spun on his hooves and ran back down the stairs, with Maya quickly joining
		 him.
		-I myself was struck (nearly) speechless.
		-The queen was big on oaths of service, a thing she was eager to push on the lot of us.
			-Lucien especially.
		-Fortunately, Lucien had thoughts. . .
			-He and our wrinkly queen here had an overlap of interests: an enimity with Lucien's
			 angelic kin.
			-There was a lot of wrangling, but he managed to sell her on the head of one of his more
			 famous kin in return for her aid getting back to The Material.
				-Definitely a win-win, as Lucien later explained that, though she's his grandmother,
				 she also orchestrated the deaths of his parents.
			-The Lich Queen _did_ set a deadline, though: within a week.
	-So, we returned to the ship and delivered the news to the others, with a decidedly mixed
	 reception.
		-Apparently some of the others are a bit more tolerant of self-righteous celestials than I.


2/10/25:
	-"What do you lot drink around here?" I asked the first githyanki I encountered outside the
	 throneroom.
	 "Well, that depends. Are you drinking to get drunk, or before battle?" he replied.
	 "Yes! . . . you know how it is: one thing tends to lead to another. . ."
		-The gith took us to a bar within their astral city, and introduced me to something called
		 "Starforged Mead".
		-Taking a swig from the bottle of sparkling liquid, it was deliciously sweet and, weirdly,
		 left me feeling. . . focused?
		-"See! I told them I should be able to drink in class. . ." I exclaimed. "Shit, my shoes
		  have to try this," I added, as I poured some down my ankle.
		-It seemed for a moment I'd offended our host, until my boots spoke up saying, "Yeah, that
		 is damned good!"
		-"Do you still have your uncle around here somewhere?" D'Roc asked.
		 "Oh! Yeah, Uncle Rov would definitely enjoy some too. . ." I replied, and then began
		 rifling through my pack. "Bottle of rum. . . empty bottle of rum. . . Ah! Bottle of uncle!"
		-The Rov-slime too got a pour, and briefly developed a set of star-like white dots. He then
		 pronounced his approval by shaping his slime-self into a thumbs up.
	-Impressed thus far, I asked the bartender what else was on the menu.
		-He asked me whether I was looking for something basic or more exotic and I claimed
		 "cosmopolitan tastes", so he offered me a silver, swirling liquid that he claimed had been
		 distilled from the essence of the Astral Plane itself.
		-I downed a dram of the quicksilver concoction and. . . found myself elsewhere.
			-I sat in something like the classrooms of my childhood in the creche, but decorated
			 with illustrations of happy animals and the like, rather than the gray, utilitarian
			 spaces I recalled.
			-It was like I drank to forget my childhood, and instead found a better one. . .
		-"Shit, guys! You've got to try this!" I said, as I bought a round for the rest.
		-I watched most of my fellows have a glass each, then each zone out for a minute or two.
	-That eventually led to some philosophical discussions with our gith guide.
		-Talking about how long we'd had our ship led to our dragon encounters, which led to the
		 githyanki alliance with the dragon god Tiamat (and some choking, then heming and hawing
		 from Maya).
		-Eventually, though, we seem to have managed to thoroughly weird out our host, who took his
		 leave of us.
	-That then left us to discuss our next move.
		-We settled on learning a bit more about Lucien's grandmother. He himself had peeled off at
		 some point on the way to the bar, so we eventually caroused our way back to the ship.
		-Lucien had beaten us there apparently, and we could hear him in his cabin sharpening his
		 sword and muttering. . . We opted to leave him be for the moment.
		-After some discussion, we decided to visit her homeplane, Aborea, and do some homework.
			-Jade claimed the Celestials operate some form of Internal Affairs service, and, if
			 Lucien's grandmother is as dirty as he says, they probably have some dirt on her.
			-Through some mix of planar knowledge and our ship's new navigation equipment, the
			 scholars and arcanists among us were able to identify a city on Aborea that we could
			 travel to, one large enough that it should offer us opportunities to investigate.
			-We did decide it would be better to arrive outsided the city and make a subtle approach,
			 as opposed to appearing in the air above it in the airship.
	-We returned to our ship, and soon shifted to Aborea.
		-We appeared hovering alongside a cliff some distance from the city, with a dense canopy
		 of trees far below us, startling some deer as we emerged from our ship.
		-That actually prompted Grimble to offer a suggestion, and soon he was fluttering after the
		 deer, aloft on his butterfly wings.
		-They seeemed rather less alarmed by him flying than us stomping, and soon he was conversing
		 with them in a simple language known to his forest-dwelling people, one with which they
		 could communicate with creatures of the forest. In short order, he had them eating bits of
		 rations from his hand.
		-They informed him of both ways down to the forest below, and also dangers.
			-To the North, a winding slope led downward, but they'd also seen a lion?
			-A nearby cave led down more quickly, and had tasty food, but also smelled of a nest?
		-We opted for the Northern route, and set out.
	-As we walked on through the wilderness (a weirdly diverse wilderness, with different
	 environments abutting one another, desert next to jungle, far more abruptly than we'd see on
	 The Material Plane), Bruce called attention to the fact that we were being hunted.
		-After a whispered conference, D'Roc, with my advice, attempted to lead us to a place that
		 would trick our pursuer into revealing himself.
		-That. . . did not work. We did a fancy loop around a big tree at the center of a clearing,
		 but instead of revealing our pursuer, that led to a bolas flying out of some nearby
		 vegetation.
		-That led to a short scuffle with some sort of lion man.
			-We spotted him where the bolas came from, and Grimble blasted the great tree, causing
			 it to crash down between the us and him, before darting behind some rocks.
				-Or, as it turned out (and we saw once he dispelled it), created the illusion of
				 all that happening!
			-I darted for cover myself as I cast my mind forward in the future to anticipate the
			 threat.
			-The others similarly took up defensive positions as a lion-man hybrid emerged from
			 the vegetation. . . and let loose a painful, deafening roar.
			-Bruce conjured a ramp of stone up to the embankment on which the lion man stood and
			 D'Roc ran up it shouting threats.
			-The lion man then dived back into the vegetation, but Sarge drove him back out by
			 blasting the area with a ball of fire.
			-I'd been waiting for his reappearance, though, and, catching sight of him again,
			 focused my mind on him and soft-locked his brain, leaving him at our mercy for as long
			 as we wanted.
		-My mental powers left the creature helpless, but also me less than helpful and him unable
		 to speak, so our next order of business was to secure him in a different manner.
		-Ultimately we settled on encasing him in salt, conjured by Bruce, and having D'Roc standby
		 with his axe.
		-I then released his mind and, after some momentary disorientation, he (the mane made it
		 plenty clear) was demanding his release.
			-We eventually calmed him down a bit and he explained that he'd been hunting the deer
			 when our airship's arrival scared them off, so he decided to hunt us instead. . . though
			 he swore he only wanted to talk. . .
			-"You're supposed to open with a 'Hello' or 'How are you doing?'. Not a bolas from the
			  bushes!" I repremanded him. "I should know! I'm an expert diplomat!"
			-Well, I did go on to admit I understood being hangry and that, though my rations were
			 mostly hardtack and similarly awful shit, I did have some rum!
				-He seemed unfamiliar with the concept!
				-He asked if this beverage came from a stream or pool or. . .
				 "It come from sugar cane!" I explained.
				 "And this 'sugar cane' was defeated in glorious combat?"
				 "Well, I do think there's some beating of the cane involved. . ." I said. "And
				  distilling! Here. . . let me pour you a glass."
				-He gulped down his dram and, coughing and sputtering, shouted, "Gods! The stuff is
				  awful!"
				 "Well, it _does_ fight back. . ." I offered.
				 "Still. . ." he went on. "It does seem to have a rather pleasing effect on
				  oneself. . ."
				 "That it does! Here, have another. . ."
			-Soon, we were on much friendlier terms, and had learned his name was Kaelith.
			-We explained were were here seeking the nearby city, come to visit some kin of a friend
			 of ours.
				-"Oh! So he's a Celestial?" Kaelith asked.
				 "His ancestry comes from all over the place," I allowed.
				 "Where is this friend?"
				 "Back at our ship," D'Roc offered. "Preparing. . . a gift for his grandmother."
				 "So. . . you're some kind of scouting party?" the lion man asked.
				 "You could say that," I said. "Sometimes you have to flush out your quarry after
				  all. . ."
			-He offered to lead us to the city, which he named Canopy's Reach, though his finger
			 wouldn't hold quite steady when he tried to point in it's direction.
	-His intoxication aside, we followed our erstwhile pursuer to where he said the city lay.
		-Eventually, the sunlight dimmed and we made camp for the evening, Kaelith, D'Roc, and Bruce
		 constructing a campsite and improvised shelters for us all.


2/24/25:
	-Lucien caught up with us as we were drinking around the campfire, to some alarm on Kaelith's
	 part at our horned companion emerging from the darkness.
		-We calmed him down, though, letting him know Lucien was another of our companions.
		-More drinking ensued. . .
	-Come morning, we continued on to the city.
		-Conversationally, Kaelith asked us if we thought they'd let us through the city's walls.
		 "Well, I did until now," I responded.
		-Nonetheless, we continued on, until the city's enormous stone walls were in sight.
		-At which point, Kaelith said he'd made good on his word, as indeed he had, and asked for
		 a parting gift of rum, brandishing an empty waterskin.
		 "Just say when!" I happily replied, filling the bottle to overflowing, luxuriating in my
		 infinite rum, until he actually did.
	-No one greeted us at the gate, but D'Roc banging away at the thing sorted that.
		-After an exchange of "Who goes there?!?" and what not, we got to explaining that we were
		 here in search of our friend's long lost kin.
		-The gate guard was quite skeptical of us, particularly eyeing Lucien's horns (and giving
		 D'Roc a great deal of offense when he said as much).
		-But, I was able to convince the guard of our good intentions, and he eventually let us
		 through the gates.
		-He _did_ though insist we check our weapons as the gate, leading to some frantic scrambling
		 to conceal blades and the like.
			-I myself happily handed over my (cheap) weapons, though I "explained" that my wands
			 were wands of, "Cure Light Wounds, Cure Moderate Scabies, Heal Some Other Stuff. . .
			 I'm a healer you see!"
	-We needed information to get more information, so we started by asking around the market.
		-"Such nice people here. . . How do you keep them so?" and similar, angling for that
		 "Internal Affairs" service we'd heard the celestials maintained.
		-Ultimately, we ended up bribing a merchant who was clearly fishing for it, and also liquored
		 him up (naturally).
		-With Lucien mentioning his grandmother's name (which I promptly forgot), the merchant was
		 indeed aware of rumors of a scandal involving a grandson. . . and also some kind of super
		 soldier program: warriors trained by air elementals or something like that, whirlwinds of
		 blades.
	-Taking our leave of our notably corrupt corruption expert, we found a bit of privacy to discuss
	 our next move.
		-Lucien was immediately thinking about how to sneak into the temple in which his grandmother
		 worked or resided or whatever.
		-I, though, proposed trying to lure her away from it somehow, some of us (here I was eying
		 D'Roc) not being the sneakiest folks in the world. . .
		-Lucien then proposed announcing his "capture", and trying to lure her back to the boat to
		 come take possession of the "prisoner".
		-I had an alternative in mind, though: quinceanera!
			-This required explaining. . .
			-Essentially, I proposed throwing some kind of party in Lucien's honor, in an effort to
			 both lure his grandmother there and provoke her.
	-Weirdly, the quinceanera thing kept snowballing. . .
		-We visited a party shop in a tree, run by fairies, to purchase streamers, cupcakes, banners
		 for confusing assortment of conflicting events, and a bunch of self-playing kazoos.
			-Sadly, Maya was not with us, as this totally would have been her kind of thing. I think
			 she was sulking a bit, due to this whole hunting angels and allying with Tiamat's allies
			 thing. . .
		-We then debated a location and, even more weirdly, I convinced myself, then the others, that
		 the ominous cave the deer were telling us about was a great location.
			-I mean, it _was_ near to both the city _and_ our ship, it was outside the city. . . and
			 it made me giggle.
		-On our way to scout the location, we also took some time to spread rumors about the upcoming
		 party:
			"It's going to be the event of the millenia. . ."
			"The Material Plane's famed Party Lizard might even make an appearance. . ."
			"You probably haven't heard about it yet. . . it's really underground."
	-So, we had D'Roc look for the end of the cave system nearest the city, a thing he did with
	 obvious ease.
		-The opening he lead us too required some sqeezing from his large form, but nonetheless he
		 lead the way. . . and called a halt just inside.
		-He and Lucien explained that the loose sand ahead of us. . . with skeletal hands poking
		 out of it. . . posed a hazard to us.
			-Duh.
		-Thankfully Grimble and Sarge were easily able to sort that, glassing the sand with a
		 judicious application of conjured flame.
		-Soon, we had a neat glass floor for the entrance, complete with spooky skeleton hands
		 underneath!
		-I found myself curious if that had drawn any attention to us and, sure enough, cocking his
		 head, D'Roc said he could hear some. . . squawking, coming from deeper in the cave.
		-Hearing that, Lucien scouted forward while Grimble and I took up defensive positions, hiding
		 behind a rock outcropping.
		-The rest of the party crept forward too, and, apparently seeing something down a hole,
		 Lucien raised his blade, ready to attack it, while Sarge blasted the ceiling above the hole,
		 dropping rocks down it to much further squawking.
		-Soon, some kind of bird-horse emerged from a different hole.
		-Grimble blasted it with a ball of fire while I loosed some arrows at it, then Lucien ran
		 forward and cut it in twain.
			-"It's cooked! . . . And smells pretty good," I added.
			 "Party appetizers!" D'Roc suggested.
			 "Yeah! . . . Anyone know if it's unethical to eat. . . whatever that is?" I ssked.
		-There were still plenty of bird noises echoing through the cave so Sarge and D'Roc rushed
		 forward to join Lucien while I asked Grimble for some invisibility and crept forward myself.
		-Soon, another of the creatures soared out from the same hole in the cavern floor.
		-I loosed another arrow at it as it swooped at Lucien, the arrow hitting but it thankfully
		 missing Lucien, continuing past him as the devil-angel-man-whatever swiped at the
		 horse-bird-whatever with his blade.
			-(I'm not trying to give offense! Fuck knows whatever _I_ am. . .)
		-Lucien ran after the creature and lept onto it's back, sinking his blade into it's flank.
		-It fell to the earth, dead and bleeding, but unfortunately slipping into one of the nearby
		 cracks in the cavern floor. . . with Lucien sliding in after.
		-Fortunately, Jade's artifice meant I was hasted, so I rushed forward and tossed him a
		 rope. . . though my effort to wind it around a nearby root just ended up breaking the root,
		 and with me sliding toward the pit myself.
		-Thankfully, Grimble rushed forward to take hold of the rope too and we were soone joined
		 by Sarge as well, and the three of us were able to haul Lucien back up.
	-After that, we took some time to survey the cave, collecting various trinkets from the
	 hippogriffs' victims, while Lucien victimized one of the beasts in turn, butchering and cooking
	 it.
		-(Someone informed me what they were. I also learned they are delicious. Celestial animals
		  taste _good_!)

3/10/25:
	-So, we proceeded to discuss the party plans. . .
		-My main priority was locating a suitably large depression in which to create a punch pool,
		 using my infinite rum bottle and whatever other flavors were on hand.
			-Lucien sagely suggested pouring some Abyssal Temptation in, to which I enthusiastically
			 agreed. Twice-spiked punch!
			-I located a suitable depression near the entrance, so people could fill their glasses,
			 buckets, or whatever as they came in, and began pouring. . . which continued for 45
			 minutes or so.
			-Lucien indeed poured in two bottles of Abyssal Temptation too.
		-D'Roc saw to roasting those hippogriffs, fashioning a fire and spit and carefully tending
		 the roasting horse-bird meat.
			-Grimble contributed his alchemical skill to creating an assortment of sauces.
		-Maya and Jade finally joined us from the ship when we ran back to it for supplies.
			-Jade mentioned a suitable occasion celebrated on the plane, some night of revels, that
			 we could also use as a party excuse.
			-Maya, getting into the spirit of things too, started directing bits of the prep and
			 decor to suit our noble elven-ish guests.
		-We were even joined by Kaelith and some of his lionel brethren, having heard the rumors
		 and smelled the meat cooking.
			-We talked them into playing security for the party (though reassured them that
			 definitely didn't preclude partaking of the punch).
				-"I like my bouncers like I like myself," I said. "Pretty drunk."
		-We also opted to make the party a masquerade too.
			-For my own costume, I decided to pour Uncle Rov onto my face, asking him to take
			 advantage of his slime-self-shaping abilities as suited him, for my mask.
		-We even spent a bit of time actually planning the murder, deciding to make our stand, and
		 introduce our guest of honor, on a raised bit of the cave floor near the tunnel leading
		 back to our ship.
			-Lucien mentioned his grandmother would probably bite at rumors about both her shameful
			 kin _and_ the resulting murdering of her daughter, and suggested spreading them around
			 the party.
	-We settled on tomorrow for the date of the party, and began distributing invites with the help
	 of the lionel.
	-We spent the intervening time resting in the cave system while D'Roc tended to his meat.
	-By midmorning the next day, people were already lining up outside and soon filtering inside.
		-I pressed our guests to indulge themselves at the punch pool, set up a quartet of gnomish
		 bards for music, and took some pixie powder (or whatever it was) from a pouch one of our
		 guests had.
		-Soon the party was in full swing, and I was too.
		-Busied myself spreading slanderous rumors about Lucien's grandmother, Leansia, and her
		 family. Some of them were even true!
	-Eventually there was some commotion at the entrance, some haughty elf-like lady pushing her
	 way in past the bouncers, but D'Roc went to address the matter.
		-The problem person, an elf-looking lady who, though scantily clad and apparently unarmed,
		 clearly moved like a warrior.
		-She and Lucien got to arguing. . . which soon turned into an especially aggresive dance
		 battle.
			-This party was amazing!
		-Lucien seemed to get the better of the dance-battle. . . but, then again, the walls seemed
		 to be melting.
		-Either way, the lady stormed off in a huff, with Lucien following a few steps behind
		 growling arguments and accusations at her.
		-Arguing turned into fighting, and thankfully the lady was unarmed as she was fast as fuck.
			-Faster, even, than the thankfully _armed_ Lucien.
		-I employed my precognition (which said shit's about to go down at this party) and ducked
		 behind a rock.
		-Maya tried to calm things down, but our fast foe proved immune even to her considerable
		 charm.
		-D'Roc though stepped between the pair and demanded she calm the fuck down, which at least
		 got her to turn around and begin storm out, yelling a "Your grandmother will hear of
		 this!" as she did.
		-Not content with that, Bruce, Lucien, and Maya all called out arguments concerning how
		 Lucien was clearly wronged by his grandmother.
		-Shockingly, the force of all that _did_ seem to calm things down, and the lady even paused
		 for another drink.
		-Shit, I think Lucien even began trying to chat her up.
			-Maya was naturally all about this, and even commissioned an illusory "Kiss the birthday
			 boy!" tunic from Grimble.
		-Yep, pretty soon they were making out. Well, OK, fine, a kiss on the cheek.
		-She did agree to go fetch his grandma, and took off shortly thereafter.
	-That confrontation seemed to sour the mood of some of the party goers, who started heading home.
		-Many of those that remained seemed _excited_ by the confrontation, though, if anything.
	-An hour or so later, we got word from the bouncers: Leansia had been sighted at the door.
		-Lucien walked forward to the town-side entrance, and confronted her.
		-The two of them began talking in heated tones, though I maintained a respectful (and safe
		 distance), not hearing much of it.
			-Though that didn't stop me from shouting "You tell her!" and the like. . .
		-The debate went on for some time. . . and even managed to shake Maya's faith in the
		 goodness of the multiverse. :(
		-Maya clearly didn't _entirely_ lose her faith in goodness and justice, though, as she
		 shuffled over to me and showed me some shining silver fabric in her pack: the cloak Bahamut
		 had given her to take Edric to court.
			-"Fred, it sounds like Leansia needs to face justice. . ." May began.
			 "Say no more!" I slurred, taking the cloak from her. "Grimble! Hide me!"
		-Grimble scurried over to me and, with a gesture, some arcane syllables, and a tap from the
		 gnome, I was soon invisible and creeping towards Leansia.
		-Well, I may have had more rum than was adviseable for creeping, and kept bumping into
		 things and tripping over the uneven cavern floors as I approached, but Maya attempted to
		 distract the celestial grandmother while I attempted to pretend to be a drunk pixie.
			-The former didn't work. . . but, shockingly, the latter did! Well, I guess it's
			 honestly not that far off who I am. . . especially after all that pixie dust.
		-Once close to Leansia, I lunged forward and wrapped her in the cloak.
		-In the blink of an eye, we were elsewhere, standing before an enormous silver dragon
		 sitting at an enormous desk.

4/7/25:
	-Bahamut's paralegal greeted us, saying, "Oh! You're back! What's happened now?"
		-I proceeded to explain that, "Well, mixed interplanar family, grandmother murders mother. . .
		  A whole sordid story, crying out for justice, and, well, we naturally thought of you lot!"
		-Well, the clerk made some noises about paperwork he'd need to attend to, and left us to
		 wait in a featureless void.
			-"So, drinks, then? I've got some rum!" I offered, to wide assent.
			-Jade was all business, though, and turned to some papers of her own, some designs she
			 was working on.
				-Asking her about the subject, she said it was her air-elemental-cruelty-free
				 airship engines she'd proposed, a project I enthusiastically commended her on.
		-In three drinks or so, the clerk returned. . . seeming a bit flustered.
			-Apparently, expert filer though our scaley bureaucrat claimed to be, the paper work
			 was all chaos.
			-"In fact," he elaborated, "The plane itself is. . . a bit wonky. You see, Bahamut is. . .
			  not here at the moment. The plane, then, is tightly linked to it's god."
		-He eventually admitted we could perhaps help him with that matter, help him to find his god.
			-Apparently Bahamut was known to wander, and had gone to visit an outdoor market North
			 of Vanguard Keep that he was fond of, but had been gone unusually long.
			-We agreed to help and, after a brief discussion of transit and the safety of our ship,
			 he shifted us back to The Material Plane, just outside the market.
				-My crew was with the ship, and the lion men were thankfully about as well. I figured
				 they had good reason to regard us fondly, as did many of the other partygoers.
		-Before he took his leave of us, I asked him about how we should get back.
			-"Don't worry. Bahamut can easily return you to his plane," the dragon-clerk said.
			 "What about a way back, or to get in touch, if the situation is. . . more complicated," I
			 clarified.
			 "Well, you still have the cloak. . . that can take you back there," he replied.
		-That was good enough for me, and soon the dragon was gone.
	-"Well, if you look over yonder," I began, "That looks to be a bar. Shall we start there?"
		-I greeted the bartender and asked what she was pouring.
		-When she replied mostly wine, I asked for the house red, saying I had a theme going, while
		 gesturing to my clothes.
			-What I received was a _very_ oaky red wine, near brandy-strong. Bit abrasive, but good!
		-Eventually, we got around to asking about our quarry, inquiring about an elderly man
		 accompanied by his birds.
		-She'd indeed seen an old man with seven yellow birds. He'd been touring the market's
		 various venders of magic trinkets.
	-Our next stop then was a nearby wagon with an array of items marked in draconic runes and the
	 like.
		-Our old man had indeed been there, and purchased a number of items, paying all in platinum,
		 but seemed particularly interested in a lantern.
			-It was no ordinary lantern, he clarified (of course not), but a one-of-a-kind work of
			 magic which is said to show the bearer the path to his heart's desire.
			-Well, that potentially complicates things, as who knows where that would lead a dragon
			 god. . .
		-Fortunately, Jade provided a very reasonable suggestion, that boiled down to, have you tried
		 magic?
			-She fell to leafing through tomes she drew forth from her pack, muttering, "Perhaps a
			 sending. . . Or divine communion?"
		-While Jade debated her options, Maya addressed her little dragon familiar, asking if he
		 perhaps had a way of seeking out his divine draconic forebearer.
			-The critter at least suggest he could try tracking him, picking up his sent and such,
			 a project D'Roc quickly joined him in.
			-They were indeed able to follow some footprints and the scent of an elderly man, leading
			 off from the magic vendor's wagon and into the woods.
	-We followed the tiny dragon and the enormous bull-man into the woods, until they called a halt
	 well out of sight of the market.
		-They pointed out where the footsteps stopped, becoming instead scuffed earth and crushed
		 vegetation, as if our quarry fell to the earth.
		-"Shit! How deep do you think the old-man shape goes?" I asked in alarm. "D'you think he
		 broke a hip or something?!?"
		-That was met with shrugs, but D'Roc at least had a theory of what led to the fall: a snare.
		-Several of us then looked about, including up, for evidence of our trap, and noticed
		 something funny about a large tree looming over the site of our scuffle.
			-A section of it was dead and warped, as if it had been caught on the edge of some magic
			 effect.
			-"Shit! You're saying the tree was involved?!? I know the leafy motherfuckers couldn't
			 be trusted. Don't have 'em where I'm from and I've been nervous around 'em since
			 getting here! Could fall on you any moment!" I rambled.
			-I was a bit put out that no one appeared to be paying much attention to my ranting,
			 but their discussion of the nature of the tree's damage and anti-magic fields bore
			 fruit: they were pretty sure such a field had damaged the tree and been used to trap
			 our dragon god in the form he'd shapeshifted into.
				-". . . Aren't several of _us_ magic? Is this shit unhealthy?" I asked. "Jaspar!
				 How are you doing?"
				-To my great dismay, my shoes did not respond. . .
				-Perhaps even more concerning, when I consoled myself with a swig of my rum bottle,
				 it didn't refill!
		-With that element of the trap in mind, I suggested, "Can't those of you arcanely-inclined
		 examine magic traces and the like? There something you can learn from this?"
			-Indeed, it turned out, they could!
			-A combination of Jade and Maya were able to follow traces of magic away from the scene
			 of the kidnapping, which lead up into the air, something about it's motions saying to
			 Jade "airship".
			-Thankfully too, Jaspar began to respond once we were some distance away, though he
			 described a terrifying experience of blankness.
			-Checking my rum bottle, it had also refilled, though another swig tasted. . . harsher?
			 Less well-aged perhaps. . .
				-"Those motherfuckers! They'll pay for this! They've made an enemy for life!" I
				 shouted.
	-We followed the aerial trail some distance overland, until it reached a cliff face.
		-With Maya possessed of both wings and Detect Magic, she was able to fly up and see that
		 the trail led to a cave in the cliff, high above.
		-With some short debate, we all found ways to either fly or climb up the mountainside,
		 reaching the cave.
		-Looking inside, we could see it was in fact a concealed airdock inside the cave, with
		 tunnels leading deeper into the mountain, an airship sitting there at rest.
			-A _rather nice_ ship, with a fancy-looking dragon figurehead on the front. . .
			-It _does_ help to have a back up ship, as we've established several times, and,
			 well, I _am_ a pirate. . .
	-Perched at the mouth of the cave, D'Roc warned us that he could hear a guard or the like,
	 partroling a regular path within, somewhere past the airships bulk.
		-After some whispered debate, Grimble rendered everyong within ten feet of D'Roc invisible,
		 and we stumbled forward as a ball of lunatics, clanking rather loudly in our armor and such.
		-That. . . did not fool the guard, who rushed forward to investigate and turned out to be a
		 githyanki.
		-Maya attempted to address the matter through charm, foresaking the invisibility for some
		 arcane syllables, and soon she and the guard were good friends.
		-That, though, simply lead to the guard pulling her aside and shouting, "Look out! Something
		 is creeping up behind you!"
		-He hurled a vial of what turned out to be alchemist's fire at our feet, as we all rolled
		 away from D'Roc, trying to dodge with varying degrees of success and losing our invisibility.
		-Maya was quick to explain that we were in fact her body guards, resulting some apologies
		 from the guard.
		-She was quick to interrogate her new friend, learning that nine of his fellows were deeper
		 inside the mountain, and had indeed captured an old man. He was even willing to sketch us
		 a quick map to them.
		-We thanked him for his help and promised to put in a good word with his superiors on his
		 behalf, then followed his map into the tunnels.
	-We were no more successful trying to silence our clammor as we moved through the tunnels, so it
	 was no surprise when we were soon met by another two githyanki guards, brandishing greatswords
	 and shouting warcries.
		-Thankfully, axe and spell made short work of that all.
	-Following our map, we eventually felt our various bits of magic fail us, we having found the
	 anti-magic effect.
		-But, interestingly, my psionic precognition _did not_ fail, though things got a bit. . .
		 static-y.
	-Shortly thereafter, we emerged into a chamber in which an elderly man sat in an iron cage of
	 fine meshwork, chatting with seven yellow birds.
		-D'Roc had no trouble wrenching the cage's door open, despite it's lock, and soon the man
		 was free, and greeting Maya.
		-I asked if the lamp had led him to what he wanted, and he replied that it was instead cursed.
			-"I figured," I replied, "But figured I should check. I don't judge, and who knows what
			 you're into."
		-We quickly made to leave, and as soon as we were past the anti-magic field, old man Bahamut
		 whisked us off the plane and back to his court.


4/21/25:
	-We found ourselves waiting before Bahamut's paralegal (something that sounded like Susan?),
	 Bahamut nowhere in sight now.
		-The courts back in order, Susan now asked us what god we wished empaneled to hear our case,
		 triggering much debating and recapping among our party.
			-I pointed out that we were looking for _harsh_ justice, given both Lucien's _very_
			 personal interest in the matter and that deal we made with that lich queen.
			-Maya said Bahamut was known for his mercy and such, rather not what we were aiming for
			 here, but that Cuthbert was the god of retribution.
			-We decided to defer to Lucien here (again, given the personal nature of the case), and
			 he called for Cuthbert.
		-Susan then raised the matter of witnesses we might like to call, leading to yet more debate.
			-Apparently this is the kind of court that accepts the testimony of ghosts, leading to
			 some kind of fun divination ritual in which Lucien got to experience the death of his
			 mother firsthand.
				-". . . Need a drink after that, Lucien?" I said, offering the rum bottle.
				 "I. . . will save my getting plastered until after the trial," he replied.
				 "Well, suit yourself!" I said, taking a long swig.
			-I also suggested that Gramma Lucien also made a confession of a kind at the party,
			 proposing that we call someone who witnessed that.
				-"While I myself _never_ lie. . ." I began, only to be drowned out by guffaws.
				-"Ahem. You, hit it off with that scary lady, right, Lucien?" I tried again. "She
				  seemed a kind of credible. . ."
	-Our preparations made, we suddenly found ourselves standing in a courtroom, three gods
	 presiding.
		-Two appeared as elderly men, though, armored and with his trademark cudgel, Cuthbert was
		 unmistakeable.
		-The other was more simply attired and I heard Bruce reverently whisper the name Obad Hai.
		-The third appeared a young man, shirtless and bemuscled, who Maya named Kord, God of
		 Strength.
	-Lucien, as the accuser, was asked to give the opening statement.
		-He quite eloquently laid out the case that his _cowardly_ grandmother killed her daughter,
		 not in war, but to save herself _embarrassment_, enlisting the aid of her very enemies,
		 the family of his daughter's lover, in the murder.
			-"That sneaky politician!" I shouted, from the gallery.
			 "There will be silence from the peanut gallery," Obad Hai pronounced.
			 ". . . Wait. There's peanuts? Grimble, see if we can get a bag. . ." I rambled.
				-Obad Hai waved his hand and a peanut plant sprouted from the bench beside me and,
				 with a little bow of thanks, I dug in.
	-Our celestial murderer then issued her response, going on about the shame and disappointment
	 she'd been afflicted with by her daughter's acts, the response it demanded, and how one did
	 what she had to do.
		-It was hardly convincing, with only Kord, Mr. Might-Makes-Right, seeming the least bit
		 receptive.
	-There was then some back and forth concerning how much control she really had over the demons
	 who were involved, and how this had been _supposed_ to go down.
		-She sort of alleged she hadn't _really_ meant to cause her daughter's _death_.
		-Lucien convincingly condemned her actions, and pointed out she then proceeded to _conceal_
		 these acts she now claimed were oh-so-justified.
			-I mumbled my approval through a mouthful of peanuts.
	-Grandma Celestial (as is becoming clear, I forgot her name) then called a witness, a soldier
	 that had been under her command and was there for the death of Lucien's mother.
		-He told a sob story about what a bloodbath it was, but it was hardly relevant given that
		 she's the one who set the whole mess up in the first place (a fact I couldn't resist
		 pointing out from the gallery).
	-Our triumvirate acknowledged the testimony given and then disappeared from sight, beginning
	 their deliberation.
	-Returning a few moments later, Obad Hai pronounced the judgment, saying that her conspiring
	 with demons was vile. . . but not murder.
		-Instead, he named it a most severe form of manslaughter, a thing which the consequence is
		 not death, but exile.
	-The sentence made, Lucien's grandmother disappeared from sight, and a moment later we too were
	 elsewhere, back to Susan the scaly paralegal.
		-Looking at her papers, she said, "I see you had a good outcome. .. "
		 "The peanuts were good. . . but there was no justice to be had!" I announced.
			-That occasioned a quick discussion about whether they could be improved with the use
			 of Flumphs' Blue Salt, and if the god of nature would be amenable to a business deal.
		-"Excuse me," Maya then interjected. "She was exiled. . . Exiled to _where_?"
		 "Oh," Susan said. "To the in-between. A nothingness between the planes, where she will be
		  alone with her thoughts. . . Some say there are creatures there, but presumably just
		  those sentenced to such an exile."
	-That left us to debate where next to go.
		-Jade was eager to resume her labors on various magical projects, and for the reagents she
		 required to do so. A pile of treasure burning a metaphorical hole in our literal pockets
		 and various magical dreams meant we were all in enthusiastic agreement.
			-Maya also volunteered that she had plenty of money back in Sasserine.
		-I did point out, though, that we needed to retrieve our ship, and get it back to someplace
		 useful, which meant unwinding several things, most noteably our deal with the lich queen of
		 the Githyanki and the navigation system we were promised for a thing we argueably
		 accomplished.
		-That elicited it's own agreement and so Susan waved a claw in an arcane gesture.
	-The platinum cloak's spell thusly ended, we found ourselves returned to the party, which had
	 grown quite raucous, though it was mostly the lion men that remained, dancing in a conga line,
	 brawling with each other, and continuing to work their way through the punch pool.
		-Lucien's wild-haired dance partner remained too, though, and swiftly approached us, saying,
		 "I had a feeling you'd be back."
		 "Of course!" I replied. "The party's still going!"
		-She inquired as to her compatriot's fate, and we broke the news of her exile to the in-
		 between.
			-"I see. Perhaps a fate crueler than death," she remarked.
			 "But a fate deemed just by no less than three gods," I countered.
			 ". . . I see. Then. . . I suppose it must be so."
		-She then began to kvetch about the gap this left in the leadership of Aborea.
			-"Do you know how difficult it is to lead these people?" she complained. "It is enough
			  to drive one mad. . ."
			 "Perhaps," Lucien began, "It _takes_ a madman. . ."
			-I don't know why he and Jade kept glancing at me, but I _did_ sense an opportuninty,
			 and said, "Well, _I_ did get them all pointed in the direction of one hell of a party.
			  And this place does have it's upsides: fun people, one hell of a party store. . ."
			 "Can you stay here to do so, though?" our native interlocutor asked. "Can _any_ of you?"
			 "Ah, you got me there," I admitted. "My heart belongs to the air."
			-She then spoke of a tournament, one of strength, cleverness, and the hunt. Apparently
			 it's the usual way of settling such things around here.
				-Though she did say it would be a while at best before such an undertaking could be
				 put together.
					-I suspect the difficulty managing her people was a factor there.
				-Still, it's an intriguing idea, a thing we could participate in on our own behalfs,
				 or on behalf of another, as she did mention a practice of champions.
					-I wonder if The Party Lizard would be interested? We could support him, as some
					 kind of Party Lizard Party, to enact The Party Lizard Party's Party Platform:
					 party!

5/19/25:
	-Well, back at the party cave, and over some drinks with already hammered lion-men, we discussed
	 our next moves some more.
		-We also took a quick trip to town: to sell loot, and buy more snacks and drinks.
			-(And some crafting components for Jade, as I had her make my cloak even fancier, with
			  some help from that magic crystal.)
		-Maya was eager to retrun to Sasserine, and I to unwind our deal with the lich queen, so,
		 since our reward there was to be a navigation system for the ship, that seemed the thing
		 to pursue.
			-I did think to ask Jade, "Will this navigation system have a margin of error measured
			 in hundreds of miles, like Plane Shift?"
			-She explained that, no, the new engine we installed in the ship has "advanced memory
			 banks", meaning that it would be able to at least return to places it had previously
			 been with great accuracy. Handy!
	-The party had been waning in our absence, but, with our return, it was ebbing once more!
		-I found myself passing out thimbles of liquor to a cloud of tiny fairies, and got to asking
		 them if they'd consider shipboard life, seeing the multi-verse and all that!
		-They inquried about the view of the stars from the airship ("Fantastic! You're closer!")
		 and similar details, and eventually a bunch of these "Coure" signed on!
	-Sarge had a project of his own to pursue too, and one that Aborea might provide a useful
	 setting for.
		-He knew a spell that called for dragon scales, and wanted to seek some out.
		-Maya knew there was said to be an ancient brass dragon that made it's lair on Aborea,
		 though Sarge pointed out that brass dragons were generally _good_, and that "ancient"
		 means "dangerous" where dragons are concerned.
		-I, though, proposed we _bargain_ instead, maybe even acquire two dragon scale flavors at
		 once! I suggested we offer to "take care of" an _evil_ dragon, in exchange for a scale
		 shed by this noble brass one.
		-My brilliant plan was almost as persuasive as I am, so we went about seeking to do just
		 that.
		-Our first step was to find this brass dragon.
			-Asking around town, we learned that is was said that $DRAGON_NAME, the ancient dragon
			 in question, was said to "listen on the wind" for those calling out for aid.
			-Sarge proposed several wind-conjuring spells, but Maya short-circuited all that by just
			 calling out to the breeze, beseeching the aid of a mighty dragon.
			-Beloved of the dragon god as Maya is, it was perhaps unsurprising that her efforts
			 yielded a response, words in Draconic carried back to us on the wind.
			-The voice and Sarge then had an extended debate.
				-It did a lot of moralizing, and I'm not sure they actually reached any kind of
				 deal for _it's_ scale or not, but it was very big on protecting the weak and told
				 us of a marauding _red_ dragon that terrorized an island known as Acheron,
				 elsewhere on this plane.
		-So, we returned to our ship and set sail for a different layer of Aborea, the one on which
		 the isle of Acheron lay.
			-Sailing there took half a day, during which we rested up for our big show and talked
			 about the plan.
			-We settled on luring the dragon with the sight of a rich (but illusory) caravan market.
			-Grimble and Sarge asserted that red dragons love rubies, the gems being a status symbol
			 amongst their kind, so I spread rumors around the nearby towns of the "upcoming
			 market" and the presence of "Rob the Red, ruby merchant".
		-We then sailed to the location I cited in our rumors.
			-We landed the ship some distance away. D'Roc camouflaged it to blend with the nearby
			 vegetation and Lucien, Jade, Bruce, and the crew stayed behind to guard it while the
			 rest of us went to set up our ambush.
			-Grimble conjured our illusory market and the rest of us proceeded to pretend to be
			 shopkeepers.
			-It seemed I did _too_ good with the rumors, though, as all sorts of people began to
			 try and show up to this legendary market they'd heard about.
				-I none too politely informed them that their clothes marked them as unworthy of
				 the time of "Rob the Red", they being clearly unable to afford my rubies.
				-Some were _still_ intent on rushing in, but D'Roc played bouncer and threw them
				 out (in some cases literally).
			-Eventually, the people approaching the market switched to running away screaming,
			 causing us to look to the sky where we indeed saw the distant silhouette of a large
			 dragon approaching.
		-We lay in wait for the approaching beast, Grimble and I under the cover of some of the
		 (real) trees, though others took up more obvious defensive positions.
			-Sarge was first to act, conjuring sleet where the dragon flew, disorienting it and
			 slowing it's flight.
			-As it emerged from the sleet, we let loose with various projectiles and spells, to
			 varying effect.
			-It, meanwhile, flew at the also flying, also draconic Sarge, snapping at the war mage
			 and dealing grevious wounds with it's teeth.
			-It now being nearer, though, a different solution came to my mind: my mind! I proceeded
			 to replace it's will with my own. . .
			-I then forced the dragon to land and, mindful of providing a some plausibility to the
			 mind-controlled beast, I claimed I really _was_ interested in the ruby deal, though
			 I had suspected it wouldn't deal fairly.
			-Talking up the quality of the enormous rubies my ship's hold was _definitely full of,
			 I convinced/forced it to bring us to it's lair, to arrange a trade in exchange for a
			 a portion of it's horde.
		-We returned to the ship and took flight, following the beast to it's lair, which proved to
		 be in a volcano in the islands mountainous spine.
			-As we neared the volcano, our ship was buffetted by the volcanic winds, but the crew
			 and I masterfully kept it under control while I kept the dragon's mind in thrall.
			-The beast led us to it's lair, but the cave in which it dwelled, with it's rivers of
			 lava, looked a bit hot for most of us to handle, so I insisted that the great beast
			 bring out it's horde to us, to the nearby clifftop where we landed the ship, that we
			 might deal.
			-_That_ proved to be a step too far out of character for the scaly creature and, in a
			 renewed struggle of wills, the dragon broke my hold on it's mind.
			-Where more aggressive mind control failed, Maya's charm stepped in (though I think she
			 too may have been cheating a bit, with the power of her patron).
			-Wiser in the ways of dragons than I, and more polite in general, Maya was quite a bit
			 more deferential, playing to the great beast's pride and asking it to bring out just 
			 _some_ of it's wonderous treasures, which would _surely_ be more than enough to exchange
			 for our rubies. . .
			-It's suspicions roused, the dragon selected some choice items from it's horde and
			 brought them to the edge of it's fiery cave.
			-Among the treasures was a very fine red cloak, a thing that Maya politely asked if she
			 could be allowed to try on.
			-The dragon assented and Maya braved the cave mouth's heat, flying down and putting on 
			 the cloak.
			-She then. . . froze? It took us a moment to realize something was up, and the dragon
			 even longer, but eventually it insisted the she return the cloak, reaching out to take
			 it and revealing this was nothing but the _illusion_ of Maya.
			-Remembering the gems of Mislead that gnomish cleric gave us, we looked about and
			 spotted Maya flying on her eldritch wings back to the clearing where we landed the
			 ship, already some distance from the dragon and still wearing the cloak.
			-The dragon soon noticed the same and, letting loose a mighty roar, it took wing and
			 flew towards us on.
			-Grimble uttered a few arcane syllables and then slapped Sarge on the back saying, "Go
			 get him!" Sure enough, Sarge's form blurred, the work of some illusion that would
			 certainly make him harder to hit, and then Sarge took flight himself.
			-As the dragon neared us, I, in a fit of unaccustomed bravery, ran a bit forward and
			 tried to _stab_ the dragon's mind this time.
			-My reward was a nasty bite from the unphased dragon that swooped down to meet me. I
			 shan't be doing _that_ again. . .
			-While the others let loose at the dragon with spell and stone, Grimble conjured a
			 maybe-real hippogriff to charge at the dragon and rescue me, but it's claws just slid
			 off the dragon's scales.
			-Sarge proved more effective, though, as he flew forward and conjured a cone of freezing
			 cold, halting the dragon's advance and causing it to collapse where it had stood.
		-Our victory in hand, Sarge got his dragon scale(s), and, with some work on Jade's part to
		 help us endure the heat for a time, we also got the contents of the dragon's horde!

6/4/25:
	-Well, we were still due to return to the Lich Queen, but did do some dithering, not being
	 _that_ eager to do so. . .
		-First off, she's fuckin' scary.
		-Second, we didn't _exactly_ kill Lucien's grandmother, though our solution was argueably
		 better (and I do love a good argument).
		-Maya and D'Roc also pointed out that, wait, aren't the Githyanki and their queen closely
		 allied with Tiamat? Who's rather fond of "her children", the chromatic dragons. . . like
		 the red one we just killed? Shit. . .
			-Sarge even pointed out that dragons frequently _mark_ the contents of their hoards in
			 some mystic way. . . a way that perhaps another dragon could detect.
	-In light of that last, we opted to head back to that Aborean city, to unload and otherwise
	 launder our loot, before returning to the Githyanki.
		-So, we loaded our captured hoard into the ship's hold and took to the air.
		-Speaking of the air, Sarge spoke _to_ the air, whispering (with some arcane assistance)
		 to that ancient _metallic_ dragon who set us on the trail of the red, reporting that the
		 deed was done. . .
			-Cocking his head, Sarge clearly heard some response and, a moment later, he explained
			 that the dragon had marked him in some arcane manner, in an offer of future work if
			 similar foes needed slaying.
			-He also felt confident that the mark would allow _him_ to speak with the dragon
			 across even extraplanar distances, should he require, with the aid of some otherwise
			 more limited messaging spell.
		-Sarge also experienced some kind of sinister vision?
			-He spoke of some kind of room filled with flame, maybe dragon fire. . . but it wasn't
			 all that clear to me what was going on. Sounded to me like he'd been hitting the
			 Abyssal Temptation. . .
		-As we flew back, Maya also had a suggestion: what if her familiar, a dragon himself, marked
		 the loot? Wouldn't that replace the mark?
			-The tiny dragon and our various arcanists certainly seemed to think so, so he went
			 through and handled each and every gem, coin, and whatever until he reported it all
			 marked. Problem solved!
		-Well, we headed back to town anyways, since all this money was still aching to be spent,
		 unloading our loot and doing a minor shopping spree.
			-Grimble, with the help of that magic crystal, learned a new spell in 10 minutes!
				-He also picked up an assortment of spell components.
			-Jade and Maya actually did something of the reverse, running around drumming up magic
			 crafting and building tasks for themselves, to earn some more cash.
	-Well, reasons to delay exhausted, we crushed a magic stone and then us and the ship were
	 wrenched back to The Astral Plane.
		-Docking, we found ourselves at the base of that pointlessly long stair again, met by some
		 guards.
		-They led us up that branching series of staircases, _supposedly_ up to the Lich Queen's
		 throne room. . . but Bruce noticed this path differed from the one we took before.
		-He pointed that out, calling the pair of guards out.
		-They claimed she they were leading us to a different location, but were obviously
		 suspicious.
		-". . . that wouldn't happen to be a room filled with dragonfire, would it?" I demanded,
		 thinking of Sarge's vision.
		-They hemmed and hawwed, so I resorted to. . . reasoning with them.
			-"Look," I said, "We can yell, scream, and threaten, rip secrets from each other's
			 minds, and all that. . . or just talk this out and then get something to drink?"
			-I _can_ be quite persuasive, and it seemed the reputation of my formidable mind had
			 preceeded me. . . but they also feared the legendary wrath of their queen.
			-"Well, have you tried the life of a freebooter?" I asked. "The pay _and_ booze are a
			  hell of a lot better. . . and a life on the run comes with the territory anyways."
			 "We've _already_ said far too much," one of the guards responded, "We need to get
			  out of here!"
			 "Freebootin' it is, then!" I exclaimed. "Let get the fuck gone!"
		-Of course, I explained that to get out of here, we really did need that navigation system
		 that the queen had (falsely) promised us.
		-The githyanki then described a workshop that handled ship repairs and such, where such a
		 thing could possibly be had, so I said they should take us there!
		-The guards led us up a different set of stairs, into a workshop filled with githyanki and
		 arcane machinery.
			-The guards nodded over at one of their fellow astral people, one wearing a fancy monocle
			 and hunched over some kind of clearly-magic crystal, surrounded as it was by several
			 shimmering images of itself.
			-I rushed over, all bluster, yelling about a special mission from the queen, a thing
			 of great urgency, and rambling about a celestial elf that should be dead but isn't .
			-Despite my convincing (only half an) act, the githyanki engineer _shushed_ me!
				-He said something about needing to stabilize the crystal first, to which I replied,
				 "Well, need an extra set of hands? Jade! Jade here can help, our ship's engineer. . ."
				 "Not unless she knows planar algebra. . ." he said, trying again to brush us off.
				-Jade, though, stepped in and the conversation quickly began to fly over my head, as
				 it seemed she _did_ know know alge-whatnot, and began to babble about 12 dimensions
				 and the like.
				-It seemed she _was_ able to help, and the matter was quickly settled.
			-His crystal stable, I again reiterated my partly bullshit plea for urgent help with a
			 navigation system.
			-This time, I seemed to get through to him and, though he made some noises about seeing
			 our orders in writing, Maya and I convinced him the matter was both too urgent and too
			 secret, so he set out for the warehouse connected to his workshop.
			-It was a big jumble, though, and he was taking forever to find what he was looking for.
				-Bruce had magic for that problem, though! A thing that could allow all our eyes to
				 work in unison for the search.
					-Actually, that seems quite handy for life aboard ship: https://dndtools.org/spells/players-handbook-ii--80/linked-perception--2943/
				-Together, then, we quickly found the navigation console he was looking for.
			-We then made a hasty departure, along with our two new Githyanki friends, returning to
			 our ship with the navigation console.
	-Jade made quick work of hooking the new navigation console up to our ship, which left us
	 debating our destination.
		-"I know Maya is eager to return home to Sasserine," I began, "But it might be wise to make
		  a quick detour somewhere, since we should probably be worried about pursuit by the Lich
		  Queen's forces."
		-That got a lot of nodding in assent.
		-Sadly, the (former) guards were no help with that, having spent their lives in a society
		 and religion that insisted the queen had eyes everywhere.
		-Maya, though, suggested that lawfully aligned planes might be our best option for sanctuary,
		 given the nature of the Lich Queen and her ally Tiamat.
			-That was met with a big grown of disappointment from me, as such places sound boring
			 and bereft of good booze. I especially shuddered at the mention of Mechanus, which
			 sounded like a place where everyone drank oil or some such, and thankfully talked
			 everyone out of _that_ option.
		-We settled on Mount Celestia, a place that certainly wouldn't take kindly to the queen of
		 the githyanki or the goddess of evil dragons.

6/16/25:
	-With a moment's respite on this celestial plane, we spent some time discussing what we wanted
	 to do from here.
		-Ultimately, we decided to hope this brief stop would throw the lich queen off our tail, or
		 at least that she wouldn't be all _that_ intent on revenge, since we really just held her
		 to the deal she made.
		-So, we decided we deserved some well-earned rest and relaxation (and rum!) in Sasserine,
		 and shifted there, planning to remain for a bit.
